Engineering Standards Book I Revision April 2, 2002
This revision to Standards Book I includes the following documents. The attached documents replace the existing index
pages and two procedures in your Standard Book I. Please remove the original versions and replace with the attached
copies, and incorporate these standards into the way you do business. It is imperative that all changes be implemented
immediately on drawings that have not been checked.
1. Index, Rev 11 Index I, pages 1, 2, and 3
2. Engineering-Drawing Part Number Management, Rev 7 Section 3C
3. Descriptions of Engineer-To-Order Parts, Rev 3 Section 4B
Details of Changes:
Electronic File Index, Rev. 11
Revised the indices to reflect the revision ofthe accompanying procedure.
Engineering-Drawing Part Number Management, Rev 7
1. Revised the document format and changed the use of engineering part number to drawing part number and
the use ofHOOO to #000.
2. Deleted sections 3.11 Structural Engineering, 10.22 SETUP FEA, 10.23 RUN FEA, 10.24 FEA REPORTS,
10.26 STR ENG - REV & MISC, and paragraphs 4.10 and 8.4.3,
3. Added sections 3.11 Proposal Projects, 3.12 Sales Order Projects, 10.18 FEA REPORTS, 10.19 CHECK
FEA, 10.21 STRUCTURAL ENG, 10.22 REVISION - STR ENG, and paragraph 9.2.
4. Reorganized section 9.0 DRAFTINGIENGINEERING ROUTERS.
5. Revised majority of section numbers to reflect additions and deletions.
6. Revised all tables and notations in Appendix A. (minor revisions)
Descriptions of Engineer-To-Order Parts, Rev 3
1. Revised section 4.0 to incorporate description format tables.
2. Revised description formats in all tables and added notations to Tables 1,5, and 6.
3. Deleted Appendix section.
If you have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at 5883.
Distribution:

Engineering Standards Book I Revision February 11, 2002
I
This revision to Standards Book I includes the following documents. The attached documents replace the existing index
pages and procedure in your Standard Book I. Please remove the original versions and replace with the attached copies
and incorporate these documents into the standard way you do business.
1. Electronic File Index, Rev 10 Index I, pages 2 & 3
2. Checking and Back-Checking Dwgs. & Doc., Rev. I Section 2D
Details of Changes:
Electronic File Index, Rev. 10
1. Revised the index to reflect the revision to the accompanying procedure.
Checking and Back-Checking Dwgs. & Doc., Rev. 1
1. Reorganized the procedure sections 4.0, 5.0, and 6.0.
2. Reworked section 5.0 to address general checking practices applicable to the majority of drawings and
documents.
3. Reworked section 6.0 to address specific checking practices applicable to particular drawings or documents.
Section 6.0 contains additional practices relevant to the header drawings; these practices are in addition to
the general practices. The methodology for acquiring weld procedure has been revised.
It is imperative that all changes from other (outside of Drafting/Header Design) entity reviews or mark-ups are given to
Header Design for implementation. Otherwise there is no way for Header Design to know of or approve these changes.
Identity of personnel noted in the procedure are PMA (Steve Delgado), ProlE development (Sudhakar
Lakshminarayanah and Glenn Hubenak), Header Design (the header designer assigned to job), and Welding Engineer
(Richard Clarke). If you have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at 5883.

of A. land A.2 of APPENDIXA.

4, 2001
This revision to Standards Book I includes the following documents. Please incorporate these documents into the
standard way you do business.
1. Index
2. Electronic File Index
3. Engineering-Drawing Part Number Management, Rev. 5 Section 3C
4. Engineering-Drawing Part Number Management for HPM, Rev. 0 Section 3D
The items listed above replace the existing indices and procedure in your Standard Book I. Please destroy the original
versions of the indices (at the front of the book) and the first procedure (the contents of section 3C) and replace with the
attached copies. Plus, add the enclosed Section 3D tab and the second procedure behind the Section 3C contents.
Details ofChanges:
Indices-updated to reflect this revision.
Engineering-Drawing Part Number Management, Rev. 5
1. The majority of the revisions entailed removing tasks directed for HPM. The following are the old
sections removed from this procedure: 3.13,4.12, 10.28, Table 6a of A. land all of A.7 of
APPENDIXA.
2. A minor revision pertains to the description list on Section 6.2 was formatted into a table; the
succeeding tables were then revised.
Engineering-Drawing Part Number Management for HPM, Rev. 0
1. This new procedure was created to effortlessly distinguish HPM task from HPC task. This procedure is
comprised of many of the sections removed from the last Drawing Part Number Management (revision
4) procedure.
Ifyou have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at 5873.

Engineering Standards Book I Revisions I 3,2001
This revision to Standards Book I includes the following documents. Please incorporate these documents into the
standard way you do business.
1. Index
2. Electronic File Index
3. Engineering-Drawing Part Number Management, Rev. 4 Section 3C
The items listed above replace the existing indices and procedure in your Standard Book I. Please destroy the original
versions ofthe indices (at the front ofthe book) and the procedures (the contents of section 3C) and replace with the
attached copies.
Details of Changes:
Indices-updated to reflect this revision.
Engineering -Drawing Part Number Management Procedure
1. Changed procedure title from Engineering Part Number Management Procedure.
2. General revision to maintain uniformity.
3. LAYOUT DRAWING information replaced MISCELLANEOUS WORK & REVISIONS
PERFORMED BY HPM in Section 3.13.
4. Replaced DHOOO-HPM with DHOOO-LO in Section 6.2.
5. Deleted DHOOO-HPM information in Section 5.1 and in Section 8.4 (was 8.4.2); renumbered Section
8.4.
6. The majority of the changes pertain to the Appendix A tables. The tables were revised to reflect current
Move Ticket requirements; who (by) does a move ticket and when to do a move ticket.
Although the majority ofthe revision pertained to the Move Tickets, reading the complete procedure will be beneficial
and is recommended. Ifyou have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at 5873.

Engineering Standards Book I Revisions I 11, 2000
This revision to Standards Book I includes the following documents. Please incorporate these documents into the
standard way you do business.
1. Engineering & Drafting Processes For Jobs, Rev. 2 Section 2C
2. Bills ofMaterials Creation, Rev. 3 Section 3B
3. Descriptions of Engineer-To-Order Parts, Rev. 1 Section 4B
The procedures listed above replace the existing procedures in your Standard Book I; please destroy the original
versions of these procedures (the contents of sections 2C, 3B, and 4B) and replace with the attached copies. The index
will be revised and issued at a later time.
Details of Changes:
Engineering & Drafting Process for Jobs Procedure
1. In general, minor wording changes have taken place.
2. Sections 4.0 JOB DEFINITIONS, 7.0 SHAFT JOBS and 8.0 SPARE PARTS have been revised
slightly.
Bill of Materials Creation Procedure
1. Document format has been changed.
2. Removed the 4A for forced draft units.
3. Removed the 50A and 40A from the bill structure.
4. Moved the tie-rod bar into the 12A.
5. Placed the actuators and spare shipping parts into the 60A.
Descriptions of Engineer-To-Order Parts Procedure
1. Changed procedure title from ETO Part Description Formats.
2. Added several new parts and reorganized tables.
The Description of Engineer-To-Order Parts procedure was revised extensively; reading the complete procedure will be
beneficial and is recommended. If you have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at
5873.

should be done on the header drawing work order even if working from a preliminary header design.

Engineering Standards Book I Revisions I
DA~~lUary
6, 2000
This revision to Standards Book I includes the following documents. Please incorporate these documents into
the standard way you do business.
1. Electronic File Index - Standards Book I, Revision 3 Index at Front ofBook
2. Bill Materials Creation, Revision 2 Section 3B
Replace the index at the front ofyour book, INDEX I-PG 1 and 2, with the new version (# 1 above). The
procedure (#2) replaces the existing one; therefore, destroy the original version ofthis procedure (the contents
ofsection 3B) and replace with the attached copy.
Changes:
Index - Standards Book I
Added the following revision file names to the Electronic File Index
Standard Book I - Index, R2 and R3
Bill ofMaterial Creation, Rev 2
Bill ofMaterial Creation
The general structure of the document has changed drastically; most ofthe content has not except
for the following.
Forced draft units now have a 'base unit' assembly (HOOO-345A) that is composed ofthe 3A, 4A,
and 5A assemblies. This base unit assembly is a phantom assembly and will not receive a work
order.
Standard fan rings and stub-column air seals will be placed into either the HOOO-345A or HOOO-A
assemblies (HOOO-345A ifforced draft, HOOO-l if induced).
Created part HOOO-7A-AS to group the retaining air seals together; place it in the bundle assembly.
Revised the operation linking in the bundle bill to show non-painted header parts to be linked to
operation 0300 instead of0200.
If you have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at 5873.

SUBJEcr: DAT~pri126,
Standards Book Feedback I 1999
In February of this year, TQM team, CIT2 completed the HPC standard procedure books. There is a total of
four standards book: Standard Book I -Work instructions
Standard Book II, volumes I and II - Work instructions, engineering standards and
drawing references for designing and
detailing ACHEs.
Standard Book III - Header designing and detailing standards
Standard Book IV - Standard parts and assemblies
The method for gathering feedback on the issued procedures is noted on the issuance memo of Standard
Book II as "Any discrepancies within this book as well as in the previously issued Standard Books I, III,
IV, are to be copied, marked-up and turned over to the Standard Department". At this time the method for
collecting feedback is being altered.
In lieu of turning over marked-up copies to the Standards Department please begin using the following
method for making comments on or marking-up these procedures. This new method allows streamlining of
incoming comments and helps avoid duplication of comments. This method also allows for review of
previous comments by all department personnel.
Feedback books have been created for the sole purpose of collecting your comments and or contributions to
HPC standards. These books are unique in their paper color of peach and are located on the back white-top
table in area 777E.
When contributing comments or information, please remove the stapled book section, sign out on the log
sheet in the front of the book, make your comment and return the section as soon as possible. Comments are
to be clearly noted, initialed and may be made to existing comments. Suggested additions to the standards
should be noted as such and placed in the suggested book and book section.
Ifyou have any questions or comments concerning the contents, please contact me at 5873.

DATE:
ISUBJEcr: Move Tickets for Heade:;OX:wings I December 18, 1998
This memo concerns the performance of move tickets on header drawings. It supersedes the work
instruction entitled, Time & Attendance and Move Tickets in Standards Book I, only for the situation
described here. If you are working on a header drawing that does not fit the following situation, you
MUST use the instructions in the Standards Book to perform move tickets.
The situation: You are working on a header drawing, detailing or checking, and the header
design has not yet been completed.
Time Charging: Log into the work order and operation normally, per the above mentioned work
instruction.
Move Tickets: When you are ready to perform a move ticket, per the above mentioned work
instruction, inform production engineering. They will do the move ticket for you.
Currently the system is set up so that when a move ticket is performed, all previous operations are also
completed. On header drawings, this will close operations for header design, when they really aren't
complete. There is a way to do move tickets without this problem, but it is a complicated process.
Therefore, production engineering will do move tickets for drafting in these situations only.
Ifyou have any questions or comments concerning the contents contact Frank Traynor at ext. 5800.
Distribution :
J. Galvan S. Hinton G.Mokry H. Drab L. Jordy R. Medina M. Luna
R. Satterwhite P. Edwards R. Evans B. Richardson

STD BOOK SECT. 1-PG. 1
INTRODUCTION TO THE HPC ENGINEERING STANDARDS BOOKS
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 To explain what the Engineering Standards Books are and how they are arranged. It will
define what type of infonnation will be stored in each book.
1.2 To provide the location ofthe physical and electronic versions ofthe book.
1.3 To provide the location ofall supporting documents and masters.
1.3 Give instructions for revising the books. This includes adding new documents and
sections.
1.4 Responsibility for maintaining the electronic and physical versions of the books will be
assigned.
1.5 The appendix has a nomenclature table of tenns used throughout all Standards Books.
2.0 CONTENTS

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 1 - PG. 2
3.0 THE ENGINEERING STANDARDS BOOKS
3.1 The engineering standards books are a collection ofwork instructions, engineering
standards, and drawings.
3.1.1 These documents describe how work is done in the Engineering department.
3.1.2 Some ofthese work instructions define how to perfonn administrative tasks such
as recording labor transactions for different tasks.
3.1.3 Others give more general infonnation on how certain types ofjobs should flow
through the department.
3.1.4 Some of the work instructions, combined with engineering standards, defme how
engineering documents and drawings are to be created. They provide infonnation
on how Air Cooled Heat Exchangers are designed and built.
3.1.5 Lastly, these books contain drawing masters and drawings ofstandard parts that
will help reduce the drafting and engineering time associated with ACHE design.
3.2 These work instructions, drawings, etc. are segregated into five different books. Books that
become to large to fit in one binder will be further segregated by volume.
3.2.1 Standards Book I is a collection of a wide range of work instructions. It includes
several miscellaneous work instructions for how work is done in the Engineering
department. It also discusses how department personnel should interact with the
main manufacturing database being used by HPC. This includes the entering of
information into Visibility~.
3.2.2 Standards Book II will define how ACHEs are designed. This includes work
instructions, engineering standards, and drawings that will assist the Drafting
Department in designing each component of a bank of ACHEs. This will range
from thecreation oflarge numbers ofdrawings that detail the lower structural
members to the creation of letter sized documents like the Coating Sheet and Fan
Order Fonn.
3.2.3 Standards Book III contains engineering design standards, drawings, and work
instructions for the design ofthe Headers in our process bundles.
3.2.4 Standards Book IV is acollection ofdrawings ofstandard parts used inACHE
construction. These are parts that have been designed and detailed in advance of
their use on jobs.
3.2.5 Standards Book V is the Instruction Manual that is given to ACHE customers.
3.3 When there is a disagreement between one ofthe Engineering & Drafting Procedure
Changes or other Engineering documents issued previously, and any ofthese books, these
books will take precedence.

4.0 LOCATION OF THE STANDARDS BOOKS
4.1 There will be an electronic copy ofthe standards books. This includes copies of all charts,
drawings, work instructions, etc.
4.1.1 The electronic files can be found on the HPC_Houston server in Volume 2, drive
'Q'.
4.1.2 The directory path for the files is:
Q:\HPC_CAD_SERVER\sTANDARDS & PROCEDURES
4.1.3 The sub-directories are then broken down by standards book, section, and fInally
document (refer to the individual indices at the front ofeach book).
4.1.4 Supporting documents to each work instruction will be stored with it in its own
directory. Work instructions that require the use of supporting documents and/or
files will also refer to those supporting items in the body ofthe document. This
reference will give the exact file locations and names.
4.1.5 Each standards book directory will also contain a Microsoft Word~ document that
indexes that book and the directory for that book on the server. The exception to
this will be Standards Book IV, whose index is in Microsoft Excel~.
4.1.5.1 Each index is broken into two sections, one for the electronic files and
one for the hard copy.
4.1.5.2 The electronic file section will list both directories and fIles.
4.1.5.3 The names ofthe directories and files will be listed in a hierarchical
structure, similar to the directory tree.
4.1.5.4 The lines associated with directories will be preceded with a D.
4.1.5.5 The lines associated with files will be preceded with a F. The software
application associated with that file is also shown on the right side of
the page.
4.1.5.6 The book index lists every section and the names of work instructions
and other printed documents. Book sections are shown in bold face
text.
4.1.6 These electronic files will be protected against alteration. The following
personnel will have access to alter the fIles and/or change security:
Standards Department Personnel
Drafting Supervisor
Production Engineering
4.2 There will be a master hard copy version ofthese books that will be stored in the Standards
Department.
4.3 A hard copy version ofeach book will also be distributed to selected locations. These
include, but are not limited to, persons at HPC, HPM, and selected vendors. This

5.0 MAINTENANCE
5.1 Issuance of Standards Books
5.1.1 The original ofeach book will be handled by the Standards Department. The
books will be issued with a cover letter explaining what the book is and which
documents, currently in place, it replaces, ifany.
5.1.2 All older documents, regardless of revision number, should be destroyed. The
exception to this is that a copy ofthe older procedures will be preserved by the
Standards Department.
5.1.3 All procedures issued as part of a standards book will start with a revision number
ofO. This is even if that procedure had been issued separately, with a later
revision number, prior to the book's release.
5.1.4 A memo will be sent via electronic mail to all HPC personnel who have electronic
mail service. This memo will state that the book is being issued and where the
electronic versionscan be found. The memo will also state that ifcopiesofthe
books are made, their own copies may not be up-to-date ifthey do not follow
every future electronic memo.
5.2 Revisions to Documents in Standards Books
5.2.1 Ifa document in a standards bookhas to be revised, the revision number ofthat
document will be increased by 1. Only the document being revised will have its
revision number increased.
5.2.2 A hard copy will be distributed to everyone logged with the Standards
Department as having a copy.
5.2.3 A memo will be sent via electronic mail to all HPC personnel who have electronic
mail service. This memo will state which procedure in which book was revised.
It will also give the file name ofthe document and a briefdescription ofthe
revision.
5.2.4 There are some documents, such as Bill ofMaterials Creation in Standards Book
I, section 3B, that have appendices for tracking small changes to them. When

5.4.1 The Standards Department will have sole responsibility for maintaining these
books with assistance from Production Engineering.
5.4.2 They will make all necessary changes to the electronic files.
5.4.3 They will handle the issuing of the books, revisions to the books, and additions to
the books.
5.4.4 They will keep track ofdocument revisions and location ofelectronic and hard
copies of those documents.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 2A -PG. 1
TIME & ATTENDANCE AND MOVE TICKETS
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 To insure time charges in the system are accurate and timely.
1.2 To insure move tickets are done properly & timely.
1.3 This document addresses the issue ofhow to charge time and perform move tickets; it does
not address when and whom. Refer to Drawings in Standards Book I, section 3C for
information on when and whom.
1.4 Paragraph 3.0 gives a general overview of a typical day with time charging and move
tickets. It explains when to assign yourself to work and perform move tickets.
1.5 Paragraph 4.0 explains how to use Time & Attendance to assign yourselfto work.
Department 31 (Drafting) should use this procedure to charge time. There are two methods
for work assignment: job assignment and manual assignment.
1.5.1 Use job assignment for most project-related work. In some rare cases, overhead
tasks will also appear in the job assignment screens, such as TQM work.
1.5.2 Use manual assignment for revisions and miscellaneous documents.
1.5.3 There are also circumstances where you will need to assign yourself to overhead
work that does not appear in any ofthe job assignment screens. This could
include training and special projects.
1.5.3.1 Use manual assignment to assign yourselfto these kinds of tasks.
1.5.3.2 You should never assign yourselfto work other than what appears in
job assignment, revisions, or miscellaneous documents without
authorization from a Section Leader, the Drafting Supervisor, or the
Engineering Manager.
1.6 Paragraph 5.0 explains how to perform a move ticket, ifa move ticket is required.
1.7 Appendix A provides a table that lists all of the work centers and work center stations used
in the Engineering and Drafting departments.
1.8 Throughout this procedure, words enclosed in single quotation marks (' ') are the names of
actual fields in Visibility. Letters, numbers, and marks that are in bold face type are actual
Visibility inputs by the user.

3.0 GENERAL PROCEDURES
3.1 Swipeyour badge andclockyourselfinat the beginning ofyour workday.
3.2 Assign yourself to the first job of the day. Refer to paragraph 4.0.
3.3 Perfonn required work. When finished or pulled off to work on something else, proceed to
the next step.
3.4 If you completed work on a miscellaneous document or a revision, or you did not complete
the current task, skip step 3.5 and proceed to 3.6.
3.5 If you completed the current task, perfonn the move ticket. Refer to paragraph 5.0.
3.6 Assign yourself into the next job. Refer to paragraph 4.0.
3.7 Continue steps 3.2 through 3.6 until you are ready to clock yourself out for the day.
3.8 Swipe your badge and clock yourself out at the end of your workday.
4.0 TIME & ATTENDANCE
4.1 Log in to Visibility
4.2 From Main Menu, enter TA in the selection field, then <ENTER>.
4.3 If you are working on a revision or a miscellaneous task that does not have a work order
specifically set up for it, proceed to step 4.4. Otherwise, skip steps 4.4 through 4.13 and
proceed to step 4.14.
4.4 From the Time & Attendance menu, enter 07 (for Manual Assignment) in the selection
field, then <ENTER>.
4.5 The cursor should be in the 'Trans Type' field. Enter WO, then <ENTER>.
4.6 In the 'Charge No' field, enter the work order associated with the' JOB' drawing part
number, then <ENTER>. This work order number will be D####JOB, where "###" is the
project number.
4.7 In the 'Oper No' field, enter the operation number that corresponds with the task you are
about to perfonn. You can enter an *, then <ENTER> to use the look-aside screen to help
find the correct operation number. You can also refer to A.5.1 in the appendix.
4.8 Press <ENTER> in each of the following fields
4.8.1 'Work Ctr'
4.8.2 'Station'
4.8.3 'Shift Date'
4.8.4 'Trans Date'
4.9 In the 'Number' field, enter your Visibility employee number, then <ENTER>.
4.10 Press <ENTER> in each ofthe 'Labor' fields ('Opn/Code').
4.11 In the 'Clock-In' field, enter the time that you begin the job, then <ENTER>.

I
STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 2A -PG. 4
4.11.1 You do not have to enter the 'Clock-In' time for the first job. Ifyou just press
<ENTER>, this time will default to the time you swiped your badge. However, if
there is a delay greater then 15 minutes before you begin working on your first
assignment for the day, then you will have to enter the 'Clock-In' time.
4.11.2 The format of the time should be "H.MM".
4.11.2.1 H = the hour, using military time
4.11.2.2 MM = the minute of the hour
4.11.2.3 Example: 3.15 = 3:15 AM, 15.15 = 3:15 PM
4.11.3 On occasion, there may be a problem with the work order and will not be able to
assign yourself to the job until after Production Engineering can fix the work
order. In these cases, the start time may actually be prior to the current time. This
is OK for these situations. Assign yourself to the job as soon as Production
Engineer informs you that the problem has been fixed.
4.12 You should now be in the 'Number' field of the next line. Enter II, then <ENTER>.
4.13 In the 'Action' field, update the screen using DR, then <ENTER>. Proceed to step 4.26.
4.14 After completing step 4.3, the cursor should be in the 'Selection' field. Enter 13 (for 'Job
Assignment'), then <ENTER>.
4.15 The cursor is now in the 'Work Ctr' field in the Job Assignment screen. Enter the four
pieces of information listed below. Press <ENTER> after each.
4.15.1 Work Ctr:
Enter the 2-letter code for the work center responsible for the job, per table 1 in
appendix B.
4.15.2 Station:
Enter the 1- or 2-digit alphanumeric code for the work station responsible for the
job, per table in appendix B.
4.15.3 Sort by Part:
You can enter 1 of 2 values here. Enter "Y" if you want the list to be sorted by
part number or "N" if you want the list to be sorted by start date. It is suggested
that you enter Y.
4.15.4 List Planned:
You can enter 1 of2 values here. Enter "Y" if you want to see all planned work
orders. Enter "N" if you do not want to list planned work orders. Since you can
not assign yourself to a planned work order, it is suggested that you enter N.
4.16 You will see a list of 7 work orders, each on its own line. Each line consists of 2 rows.
4.17 Locate the work order and operation corresponding to the work you are about to start. Be
sure that you choose the correct work order and operation. The screen is very cluttered and
it is easy to select the wrong work order or operation.
4.17.1 The work order number is on the first row towards the left side ofthe screen. Its
associated part number is on the first row in the center of the screen.

4.17.2 The operation number is on the first row just to the left ofthe dates. The
description of that operation can be found immediately below the part number in
the second row.
4.17.3 At the far right ofthe screen is a column of numbers from 05 to 18. There are two
numbers for each line (task). The second (the even numbers) is used for assigning
yourself to one ofthose operations listed.
4.17.4 You may have to press <ENTER> several times in the 'Action' field to find the
correct operation. Ifthe operation you are looking for is not in the list, contact the
appropriate section leader immediately.
4.18 In the 'Action' field, enter the number corresponding to assignments for the desired
operation, then <ENTER>.
4.18.1 Refer to 4.17.3 for choosing the correct operation.
4.18.2 Refer to 4.11.3 if there is a problem preventing you from assigning yourself to a
job.
4.19 You will nowbe in the'Assign Crew' screen. Press <ENTER> in both'Shift Date' and
'Trans Date' fields.
4.20 Enter your employee number, then <ENTER>.
4.21 In the 'Labor Opn' field, press <ENTER>.
4.22 Enter the current time in the 'Clock-In' field, then <ENTER>. Refer to paragraph 4.11.
4.23 You should now be in the 'Employee Number' field. Type II, then <ENTER>. This will
take you back to the'Action' field.
4.24 Update the assignment by typing DR, then <ENTER>.
4.25 If you complete the current operation before moving to a new task, perform the move ticket
for that operation. Refer to paragraph 5.0.
4.26 If you have other business in Visibility you can now attend to it. If not, exit Visibility
properly.
4.27 Ifat any time you are unsure ofhaving assigned yourselfproperly, you can use the Time &
Attendance Inquiry screen to see what job you are currently assigned to, if any. The
procedures for checking current assignments are as follows.
4.27.1 Remember these procedures are for current assignments only. This screen can
also be used for reviewing past assignments. You will have to refer to the
Visibility Time & Attendance Users Manual or consult your section leader for
those procedures.
4.27.2 In the 'Action' field ofthe Main Menu, type TA, then <ENTER>.
4.27.3 In the 'Selection' field ofthe Time & Attendance menu, type 11, then <ENTER>.
4.27.4 The cursor should be in the 'Employee' field. Enter your employee number, then
<ENTER>.
4.27.5 Press <ENTER> again.

4.27.6 In the 'Charge No' field, press <ENTER>.
4.27.7 Press <ENTER> twice more.
4.27.8 In the 'Posted' field, type U, then <ENTER>.
4.27.9 Press <ENTER> again.
4.27.10 You will now be able to view all job assignments back to the last system posting.
The system will not post an assignment that has not completed so you should
always be able to see the job to which you are currently assigned. The last task
shown in the list is the task to which you are currently assigned.
5.0 MOVE TICKETS
5.1 Log in to Visibility.
5.2 From Main Menu, type TA in the selection field, then <ENTER>.
5.3 From the Time & Attendance menu, type 14 in the selection field, then <ENTER>.
5.4 The Move Ticket Entry screen asks for 3 entries. Enter each, per 5.4.1,5.4.2,5.4.3,
pressing <ENTER> after each entry.
5.4.1 Work Ctr:
Enter the 2-letter code for the work center responsible for the job, per table 1 in
appendix B.
5.4.2 Station:
Enter the 1- or 2-digit alphanumeric code for the work station responsible for the
job, per table 1 in appendix B.
5.4.3 Sort by Part:
You can enter 1 of 2 values here. Enter "Y" if you want the list to be sorted by
part number or "N" if you want the list to be sorted by start date. It is suggested
that you enter Y.
5.5 You will see a list of seven work orders, each on its own line. Each line consists oftwo
rows.
5.6 Locate the work order and operation that you have completed. Be sure that you choose the
correct work order and operation. The screen is very cluttered and it is easy to select the
wrong work order or operation.
5.6.1 The work order number is on the first row towards the left side ofthe screen. Its
associated part number is on the first row in the center of the screen.
5.6.2 The operation number is on the first row just to the left ofthe dates. The
description of that operation can be found immediately below the part number in
the second you.
5.6.3 The balance required can be found towards the right side ofthe screen. These
should always show 1. If not, contact production engineering immediately.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STDBOOK SECT.2B-PG.l
SALARIED TIMESHEET ENTRY
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 To insure time charges in the system are accurate and timely.
1.2 Paragraph 3.0 explains when to charge time and perfonn move tickets.
1.3 Paragraph 4.0 explains how to use Salaried Timesheet Entry to charge time. Departments
33 and 34 (Engineering Support and Direct Engineering) should use this procedure to
charge all oftheir time, ifrequired.
1.4 Appendix A lists overhead feature codes. These should be used for non-project related
tasks that get charged to departmental overhead.
1.5 This work instruction is to be used in conjunction with Time & Attendance and Move
Tickets in Standards Book I, section 2A.
1.5.1 Refer to this procedure when performing move tickets after completing a task.
1.5.2 You may also want to refer to appendix B in that document which lists all ofthe
work centers and work stations used in the department.
1.6 This procedure assumes that you will charge your time at the end of each business day. If
you do not, there is no guarantee that the process described in paragraph 4.0 will work.
Problems that could occur include:
1.6.1 The closing ofthe work order prior to time entry which results in your inability to
properly charge your time.
1.6.2 Having to type a date in the 'Date' field instead ofpressing <ENTER> to get the
default date (see 4.5), etc.
1.6.3 Furthennore, unless you keep a written log ofyour time (which is duplicate work
and more time consuming) you will most likely charge an incorrect quantity of
hours. This will make future time estimates more inaccurate.
1.7 This document addresses the issue of how to charge time. Refer to Drawings in Standards
Book I, section 3C for infonnation on the where time is to be charged and when to perfonn
move tickets.
1.8 Throughout this procedure, words enclosed in single quotation marks (' ') are the names of
actual fields in Visibility. Letters, numbers, and marks that are in bold face type are actual
Visibility inputs by the user.

3.0 GENERAL PROCEDURES
3.1 Perfonn your nonnal duties.
3.2 When you finish an operation, perfonn the move ticket ifnecessary. Refer to 5.0, A2 and
AS of Time & Attendance and Move Tickets in Standards Book I, section 2A
3.3 At the end ofthe day, prior to leaving, charge all time worked during that day. Refer to 4.0
ofthis document. Keep track oftime spent on various tasks as accurately as possible. It is
preferred that you record time with a 15 minute accuracy.
3.3.1 Charge time spent on all projects.
3.3.2 Charge time spent on special projects and tasks.
3.3.3 Charge time on any other exercise other than nonnal overhead. This would
include things like training.
3.3.4 Refer to appendix B ofthis document for a list ofoverhead feature codes to be
used for special tasks that are not related to a particular project.
3.4 If you encounter a problem at any point in the process, contact Production Engineering
immediately.
4.0 SALARIED TIMESHEET ENTRY
4.1 Log into Visibility
4.2 Enter LD in the 'Action' field on the Main Menu, then <ENTER>.
4.3 Enter 5 in the 'Selection' field, then <ENTER>.
4.4 The cursor should now be in the 'Employee:' field in the Salaried Timesheet Entry screen.
Type your Visibility employee number, then <ENTER>.
4.5 Press <ENTER> in the 'Date' field.
4.6 Type the total number ofhours that you will be charging in this entry session in the 'Total:'
field, then <ENTER>.
4.6.1 There are 13 entry lines. Ifyou will need to use more than those 13 lines, you
will need to charge the time in two sessions.
4.6.2 The last entry you make in each session will be a negative charge to the proper
overhead account with a feature code of890. Do not include this entry in your
total hours.
4.7 Press <ENTER> in the following fields.
4.7.1 'Dept:'
4.7.2 'Labor Code:'
4.7.3 'Journal'
4.8 The cursor should now be in the 'Charge Number' field on the first entry line.

4.9 Type the charge number that corresponds to the work order you are recording time for or
the overhead account number for your department, then <ENTER>. If entering an
overhead account number, the format should be 5000dd-fea.
4.9.1 dd = department (33 for engineering support and 34 for direct engineering)
4.9.2 fea = overhead feature code (refer to appendix B)
4.9.3 If time charged is to an overhead account number, skip step 4.10.
4.10 Ifthe charge number entered in step 4.9 was a work order, the cursor will move to the
'Opn' field. Type the operation number that corresponds to the task for which time is being
charged, then <ENTER>. Refer to Al ofthis document, and A2 and A5 of Time &
Attendance and Move Tickets in Standards Book I, section 2A
4.11 In the 'Hours' field, type the number of hours spent on the task that day, then <ENTER>.
4.12 In the 'Labor Type' field, type El, then <ENTER>.
4.13 The cursor should move to the 'Charge Number' field on the next line. Repeat steps 4.9
through 4.12 for as many times as you have charges to post.
4.14 After you have entered all charges for the day, or all that will fit on the 12 lines, you will
need to make one last charge. Using steps 4.9 through 4.12, enter a charge to the account
5000dd-890 (dd = 33 for engineering support, 34 for direct engineering). The hours for this
charge should be the negative ofthe total ofall otherchargesjust entered.
4.15 If the cursor is in the 'Charge Number' field, after entering the last charge to overhead
account 890, type /I, then <ENTER>. Ifnot, the cursor should be in the 'Action:' field.
Proceed to step 4.16.
4.16 In the 'Action:' field, type US, then <ENTER>.
4.17 The following message will appear at the bottom ofthe screen: "Update History and GL".
Type Y, then <ENTER>.
4.18 Ifyou have other business in Visibility, you can now attend to it. If not, exit Visibility
properly.

ENGINEERING & DRAFfING PROCESSES FOR JOBS
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 Define jobs commonly referred to as Fire, Replacement, Retube, Spare Parts, Shaft, and
Warranty.
1.2 Define departmental responsibilities required in handling these jobs.
1.3 Define the structure in which departmental responsibilities are performed.

1.0 PURPOSE 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1

4.0 JOB DEFINITIONS
4.1 Project-A job consisting of either a bundle(s) or ACHE unit(s) and always originating
from the Project Coordination Department.
4.1.1 Fire Job-The HPC term applied to the top priority job requiring rapid turn
around on designs, drawings and manufacturing.
4.1.2 Replacement Job-The HPC term applied to ajob consisting ofnew bundles
replacing existing ones and not consisting ofa complete ACHE unit. The new
bundles can replace bundles by HPC or other companies.
4.2 Retube Job-A job consisting ofreplacing tubes and gaskets and with an undetermined
scope ofwork until bundles are received and inspected at the HPC manufacturing facility.
4.3 Shaft Job-A job consisting ofa fan shaft assembly requiring minimal engineering and
drafting effort and originating from the Fan and Part Sales Department. Total required
labor for engineering and drafting is usually less than one hour. If the time is expected to
take longer than four hours, the job should be treated as a Spare Parts Job.
4.4 Spare Parts Job-Ajob not consisting ofcomplete bundle(s) or ACHE units. The job will
include upgrades or modifications to existing structures and originate from the Fan and Part
Sales Department. These jobs may consist of loose fabricated parts that may be one or
more panels, belt guard(s), motor mount(s), mechanical parts, louver(s), etc.
4.5 WarrantyJob-Ajob consisting ofthe replacement ofdefectiveparts ormodifications to
existing parts as required by the written contract agreement Hudson Products provides each
client. Warranty jobs, as they apply to the Engineering and Drafting departments, the
Project Coordinator classifies the job into one oftwo categories:
Category 1, which is a warranty job where all engineering, drafting and manufacturing
costs are charged to a warranty account.
or
Category 2, which is a warranty job where engineering, drafting and manufacturing costs
are charged to a specific project number.
5.0 PROJECTS
5.1 The Project Coordinator submits a request for a project number to accounting via electronic
mail.
5.2 Accounting sets up the project and responds to the Project Coordinator via electronic mail.
This response should be copied to all personnel involved with the project. This should
include the following persons in the Drafting and Engineering departments.
5.2.1 Drafting Supervisor

5.2.2 Production Engineering
5.2.3 BOM Administrator
5.2.4 PMA
5.2.5 Document Control
5.3 The PMA enters the part, Dxxxx-JOB into Visibility (xxxx = project number).
5.4 Project Coordination distributes a complete job package. At the least, this should include
Fin-Fan® Specification Sheet, proposal drawing (if available), a copy ofthe electronic mail
response from Accounting mentioned above, and a cover page.
5.5 Project Coordinator holds a kickoffmeeting to discuss the requirements ofthe project.
5.6 Production Engineering requests part numbers for all drawings required as part ofthe 'GA'
package from the PMA.
5.7 The PMA enters these part numbers and Production Engineering creates work orders and
schedules these drawings.
5.8 Refer to Bills ofMaterials in Standards Book I, section 3A provides more information on
how to handle projects.
6.0 RETUBES
Follow the same steps outlined in paragraph 5.0 ofthis document.
7.0 SHAFf JOBS
7.1 A salesperson from the Fan and Part Sales department submits ajob package to the PMA.
The package should outline what shafts are required. If the PMA determines that the scope
of work will take longer than four hours, he/she should advise the salesperson to treat the
job as a Spare Parts Job and to consult the Drafting Supervisor.
7.2 If the shaft is from an older job, Document Control provides the PMA and the salesperson
with a copy ofthe older drawing.
7.3 If the shaft is not from a previous job and a new drawing is required, the PMA must consult
the Drafting Supervisor. The job package should contain all pertinent information required
to detail the new shaft.
7.4 The drawing, old or new, is checked and submitted to Document Control. The bill should
conform to Bill ofMaterials Creation in Standards Book I, section 3B with the
understanding that other components, such as base plates, may be required.
7.5 The PMA enters the part numbers. There are two types of part numbers for fan shaft
assembly.
7.5.1 The first type ofpart number is for an HPC shaft. The old part number (e.g.,
A300-101C-2) is used. The description is per Standards Book I, section 3B.
7.5.2 The second type ofpart number is for a non- HPC shaft. The part number
consists ofthe AOOOO series number (e.g., A0001). The part description format is
'SHAFT,competitor's name' followed by information required and provided by
the Fan and Parts salesperson.
7.6 The PMA inputs the BOM.
7.7 BOM Administrator checks the complete bill.
7.8 The PMA sends out the following message using electronic mail.

8.0 SPARE PARTS JOBS
8.1 A salesperson in the Fan and Part Sales department submits a request for a quote to the
Drafting Supervisor.
8.2 The Drafting Supervisor assigns personnel to develop the quote.
8.3 After the quote is complete, the Drafting Supervisor gives it back to the salesperson.
8.4 When the quote becomes ajob, the salesperson needs to create a sales order.
8.5 If the total estimated drafting hours for the job is equal to or greater than 4 hours, the
salesperson should also add the part number 'ENG-DRAFT' to the sales order.
8.6 The salesperson then gives a job package to Production Engineering and the Drafting
Supervisor. The job package should include the following information:
a. List of parts that are to be delivered to the customer (the quote)
b. Required engineering and drafting hours
c. Due dates for engineering, drafting, and manufacturing
d. Any other pertinent information that may affect what is to be engineered or
fabricated
8.7 Production Engineering schedules all engineering and drafting work.
8.7.1 If the total drafting and engineering estimated hours is fewer than four, work
orders are not necessary. Production Engineering issues electronic mail notifying
the Drafting Supervisor to charge labor directly to the sales order; skip the
remaining step of8.7.
8.7.2 Production Engineering requests parts for drafting work orders from the PMA.
8.7.3 PMA creates the parts and gives confirmation to Production Engineering when
done.
8.7.4 Production Engineering creates a work order for the part 'ENG-DRAFT' linked to
the appropriate sales order line, then adds part numbers for all required drawings
to the Kitup and Shortage List for 'ENG-DRAFT'. The work order number for
this part should be 'D' plus the sales order number.
8.7.5 Production Engineering attaches a router for each drawing and creates work
orders that are linked to the work order for 'ENG-DRAFT'. Production
Engineering issues electronic mail to Drafting Supervisor confirming work orders
are complete.
8.8 The PMA creates a skeleton BOM, if necessary.
8.8.1 This skeleton BOM may be informal.

8.8.2 This skeleton BOM is submitted to the BOM Administrator for review.
8.9 Drafting and Engineering will perform necessary work per the job requirements and
established engineering work instructions.
8.10 Drafting will submit drawings to Document Control for part entry, bill entry, and document
issuance. All ofthese tasks should follow normal work instructions with no special
instructions.
8.11 The BOM Administrator will assist Document Control, when necessary, with bill input.
This may be necessary since some jobs can be very complex and most may not follow
normal bill structure. The BOM Administrator will check the bill input and approve the
release ofdocuments and drawings.
9.0 WARRANTY JOBS
9.1 Project Coordinator or Fan and Part Sales salesperson submits a job package to the Drafting
Supervisor and Production Engineering. This package should describe the scope ofthe
warranty, dates for deliveries, and explain how labor and materials will be expensed­
overhead or project number.
9.2 Production Engineering and the Drafting Supervisor will coordinate to determine the
following things:
a. Engineering and drafting requirements.
b. Engineering work order requirements-Production Engineering creates work
orders following the criteria mentioned above and issues electronic mail to
Drafting Supervisor outlining how labor is to be charged
c. Bill requirements-Production Engineering creates necessary bills and
explains to the Project Coordinator or Fan & Part Sales salesperson what will
be placed on the sales order.
d. Manufacturing work order requirements-coordinate with Production,
Planning & Scheduling to get necessary manufacturing work orders created.
9.3 Drafting and Engineering performs necessary work per job requirements and established
departmental work instructions.
9.4 Drawings and documents are checked, scrubbed, and released to Document Control.
9.5 Ifbill entry is required, Document Control coordinates with the PMA and Production
Engineering to accomplish this.
9.6 The only difference between the two types ofwarranty jobs, defined in 4.5, is the method
ofcharging material and labor.

STDBOOKO SECT.2D -PG 1
CHECKING AND BACK-CHECKING
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 To document general practices for checking and back-checking drawings or documents.
1.2 To document exclusive requirements for checking particular documents and drawings.
1.2 To define personnel responsibilities.
2.0 CONTENTS
1.0 PURPOSE 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS 1
4.0 RESPONSIBILITIES 1
5.0 GENERAL PROCESS FOR CHECKING AND BACK-CHECKING 2
6.0 ADDITIONAL CHECKING REQUIREMENTS 3
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 Associated documents vary for each drawing and document. Reference the specific procedure
that correlates with the drawing or document in question.
3.2 The following manuals are to be used for checking and back-checking.
Engineering Standards Books I, II, III, and IV
HPC Computer Aided Design and Drafting Standards Manual
4.0 RESPONSIBILITIES
4.1 Detailer is responsible for:
4.1.1 Providing one check print to Section Leader
4.1.2 Providing complete information (e.g., details, layouts, work sheets, etc.) that was used
pursuant to completing the drawing/documents.
4.1.3 Completing all red mark changes when the checked drawing/document is returned for
correction.
CHECK AND BACK-CHECK PROCEDURE REV. 1, 2-11-02
Data Issued
By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0


============================================================

============================================================

(Standard Design Manual) - Downloaded By: David Cornealius, At: 2025-12-25 14:53
*2414807-0*
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STDBOOKll SECT.2D -PG 2
4.1.4 Making reference to all available data and determining if all red markings are correct
or incorrect.
4.1.5 Consulting with the checker regarding the detailer's corrections and resolving any
disputed correction calls. This step may be done after completing a total back-check
of all mark-ups.
4.1.6 Completing changes following discussion of disputed correction calls.
4.1.7 Reprinting the corrected drawing/document and to return it along with all check prints
and originals to the checker.
4.2 Checker is responsible for:
4.2.1 Checking in compliance with manuals listed in paragraph 3.2.
4.2.2 Returning check prints to the detailer.
4.2.3 Providing the detailer any new information used to check the drawing/document that
verifies mark-ups.
4.2.4 Consulting and resolving disputed correction calls with the detailer.
4.3 Section Leader is responsible for
4.3.1 Determining checking assignments.
4.3.2 Providing guidance and assistance to the detailer and checker.
4.3.3 Providing final determination of disputed correction calls.
5.0 GENERAL PROCESS FOR CHECKING AND BACK-CHECKING
The information in this section outlines the general steps when working with drawings and
documents.
5.1 CHECKING PROCESS
5.1.1 The checking process entails reviewing all dimensions, drawing details, layout details
and ensuring that the information agrees with the design intent.
5.1.2 Data accepted as correct will be colored over with a yellow highlighter.
5.1.3 Data not accepted as correct will be marked through or circled in red and correct data
will be inserted in red.
5.1.4 Correction comments will be clearly written; no abbreviations nor short hand
comments will be used to make correction calls.
5.2 BACK-CHECKING PROCESS
5.2.1 The back-checking process entails reviewing and verifying correction mark-ups,
completion of correction calls on to the drawing/document after they have been
checked and returned.
5.2.2 Data overlaid with yellow may be considered correct.
5.2.3 Data marked through or circled in red is considered as incorrect and requiring
correction.

6.0 ADDITIONAL CHECKING REQUIREMENTS
The information in this section are additions to the general checking process. These instructions
are exclusively applicable to particular designated drawings and/or documents.
6.1 HEADER DRAWINGS (ProlE and AutoCAD formats)
6.1.1 Header Design Package
a. Header Designer will create and check the header design package, which will
include the sketch, HEIDE born, drawing notes, cpo's, etc.
b. Header Designer will select part numbers for header items. Ifparts do not exist,
request new parts from Parts Master Administrator (PMA). PMA will notify
Header Design and ProlE development that parts have been added.
c. Header Designer will write in part numbers on the HEIDE born. For plate part
numbers, Header Designer will note whether plate unit of measure is each or
square feet.
d. Header Design checker will check part numbers on HEIDE born. If any errors
with requested parts, consult PMA and ProlE development.
e. Header Designer will provide drafting section leader with a completed and
signedheaderdesignpackage. Ifanypages ofthe header designpackage change
before issuance ofdrawing, new and dated pages will be given to Section
Leader. This will include part number changes on HEIDE born or notes.
6.1.2 Header Drawings
a. Detailer will give two copies ofthe check prints to Section Leader. (Detailer
will detail drawing from the latest header design package)
b. Section Leader will give one check print to Drafting Checker and one to
Document Control.
c. Drafting Checker will check drawing from the latest header design package.
d. Drafting Checker must discuss any changes or mark-ups to the header design
package with Header Design. All discrepancies pertaining to the header design
package must be resolved before completion ofheader drawing.
e. Document Control will scan check print for a TIF file and place the TIF file in
the Welding Engineer's server folder located at:
VOL2 (Q:)\Drawings\RICHARD CLARKE
Document Control will then e-mail the Welding Engineer and request the weld
procedure to accompany construction details. Section Leader, Drafting
Supervisor, and Header Designer will be c/c on the e-mail.

3.0 BILL OF MATERIALS OVERVIEW
3.1 Consider the assembly ofparts shown in Figure 1. This assembly will be used to explain
the bill ofmaterials structure.

Figure 1: Sample Assembly Diagram
3.1.1 Each square represents a manufactured pan. Each circle represents a purchased
part. All manufactured parts consist of manufactured and/or purchased
components connected at the next level below them.
3.1.2 The terms part, subpart, component, sub-component, assembly, and shbassembly
are all interchangeable. All items in the Visibility~ system are called parts. When
speaking ofparts, any ofthe terms just listed will often be used.
3.1.3 Components, either one or many, are parts that come together to form an
assembly. It does not matter how those parts how joined, whether welded or
fastened in some other manner.
3.1.4 Any part that consists of one or more components is an assembly. Every
assembly can also be considered a component if used on another assembly. In
this scenario, this assembly would also be referred to as a subassembly. ­
3.1.5 The terms assembly, subassembly and component are used to describe a part's
relationship to other parts.
3.1.6 In figure 1, numbers in parentheses represent the quantity of a component
required for each assembly shown above it. Quantity is defined in terms of the
unit of measure (UoM) for that part. In this example, manufactured part E is
composed of2 units ofpart h. IfpartEwere a gusset plate, then hmight
represent 1/2" thick A36 plate with a UoM ofsquare feet. Therefore, each gusset
would consist of2 units, or 2 sq. ft., of 1/2" plate.

3.1.9 Parts B, C, D, and E are merely groupings of raw material (the purchased parts),
but do not actually represent any true material. These subassemblies are only
defmed in terms of the components from which they are composed. All
assemblies and subassemblies are ultimately defined in terms of purchased parts
(the lowercase letters). All manufactured parts must ultimately consist ofone or
more purchased parts (i.e., all "roots" will end at a purchased part). The
exceptions to this are drawings.
3.2 Visibility~ structures all groupings, like those of figure 1, in terms ofparts (squares and
circles) and bills ofmaterials (connecting lines). A, B, C, D, E, f, g, h, and i are all parts.
All manufactured parts require a bill ofmaterial (BOM) to define what parts are joined to
create them. A, B, C, D, and E will, therefore, each require a BOM.
3.2.1 Parts:
3.2.1.1 Parts are identified by a unique number known as its part number (i.e.,
two parts cannot have the same number, and one part shouldn't be
listed under two different numbers). This part 'number' can actually
be composed ofnumbers, letters, and several symbols.
3.2.1.2 Parts are also defined by a description. In Visibility~ this description
can be 30 characters long. Descriptions longer than 30 characters may
be put in a separate field called the 'descriptor', also known as
'additional description'. Even though these two fields are separated by
Visibility, they combine to form one description for the part. When
procedures refer to a part's description they are referring to the
completed description.
3.2.1.3 A part cannot be used in a BOM until a part number has been added to
the Part Master. These part numbers can only be added to the Part
Master by the PMA.
3.2.1.4 Part numbers, when added, are entered as either make (M) or buy (B).
3.2.1.5 Buy parts are those for which no processing is required by HPC to get
it to the state described in the part's description. Buy parts include
BILLS OF MATERIALS REV. 0, 12-15-98

I I I
STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION [ SECT. 3A -PC. 4
bolts, plate, assemblies fabricated at Hudson Products de Mexico,
tubes, etc.
3.2.1.6 Make parts are those which require processing and are composed of
other 'make' parts and/or 'buy' parts. They include fans, tube bundles,
gusset plates, finned-tubes, etc.
3.2.2 Bill of Materials:
3.2.2.1 The single level BOM is simply a list of components, some
manufactured and some purchased, that are joined together to fonn an
assembly. This list includes the part numbers of the components of the
assembly and the quantity required to create one unit ofthat assembly.
3.2.2.2 In Visibility~, the BOM table stores the part number and quantity of
the components as well as other infonnation. This other infonnation
includes a spares factor, text, and several flags. This other infonnation
is important for Visibility~ to function properly and allow flexibility in
creating bills. They are not an inherent quality to bills in general.
3.2.2.3 An indented BOM is similar to a single level bill with the exception
that the single level bill for every assembly that is used as a component
is also portrayed. These series ofsingle level bills fonn a hierarchical
structure continuing for as many levels as necessary until only
purchased parts exist on the single level BOM.
3.2.2.4 Whenever an assembly is used as a component on a single level BOM,
that assembly's own single level BOM automatically becomes part of
the indented bill. This allows all bills to be stored as single level bills.
The indented BOM is simply a report that strings the single level bills
together. Bills are entered as single level for each assembly.
3.2.2.5 A BOM only exists in conjunction with a part. A BOM can be copied
from one part to another, but cannot exist separate from a part.
3.2.2.6 A part, when added to the Part Master, does not have a BOM. Ifa
manufactured part requires a BOM to defme its components, this must
be done separately.
3.2.2.7 A part can have only one BOM. This BOM follows that part
everywhere it is used on other bills.
3.2.2.8 Since the bill is only a list of components and gives no infonnation as
to how those components fit together, it is possible for more than one
part number to have the same BOM. Two braces differing only by
hole pattern, each composed of 10 linear feet of the exact same size
angle, would have the same BOM.
3.2.3 Figure 2 shows the bills of materials required for the assembly shown in figure 1.

3.2.3.1 Notice that the bills were listed from the bottom of figure I up. While
not required, this is a good practice for creating bills of materials.
Make it a practice to not list a subassembly in an assembly's BOM
until that subassembly has first had its own BOM created (i.e., do not
use subassembly B in assembly A's BOM until the BOM for
subassembly B has been created).
3.2.3.2 The exception to this is when creating the skeleton BOM. Some ofthe
subassemblies in the skeleton BOM will not have their own bills
completed until after drafting completes the appropriate details.
3.2.3.3 The skeleton BOM is an indented bill. It is composed of the major
assemblies that will receive work orders for fabrication and other
components that are known at the beginning ofthe job. This allows
for the creation of work orders and providc::s information as to the
structure of a job long before drawings are generated.

3.2.5 Ifpart A were used in a higher level assembly, the indented BOM for that higher
level assembly would include the above structure for the part A component, but
all levels would be incremented by one (Le., Part A would be level 1, Parts B, C,

"indenture level", is variable based on which BOM is printed. The indenture level
is NOT constant for a given part. Do not confuse indenture level with the part
entry "LvI" (refer to 6.9.7).
3.2.6 Note about reading an indented BOM: a component at a particular indenture level
is part ofthesingle level bill ofthepart with a lower indenture level printed
before it in the indented BOM.

3.2.6.2 Each is a component on the single level BOM for assembly B, printed
above them with a lower indenture level (level 1).
3.2.6.3 Part h, is printed directly above f, but is of a higher level (level 3) then
part f.
3.2.6.4 The next lower level part above both parts E and f is part B.
Therefore, the single level bill for part B is a quantity of 1part E and
1.5 ofpart f.
4.0 ACHE PROJECT STRUCTURE
4.1 _A project's requirements are listed in a sales order, which is prepared in Visibility~ by the
Project Coordination Department. Each manufactured part in the sales order must have a
BOM.
4.2 The purpose ofthe BOM is to structure the components ofthe project similarly to the way
these components will be assembled, fabricated, and purchased (i.e., assembly part
numbers will be created for groups ofcomponents which are all collected and required at a
given time). The BOM structure will have assemblies and subassemblies, such that work
orders can be created as necessary to logically control the fabrication process.
4.3 For a standard ACHE project, the sales order will probably list units, loose field items, and
several different drawings as the sales order line items. This will be detennined by the
BILLS OF MATERIALS REV. 0, 12-15-98

By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0

I I I
I
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 3A -PG. 7
scope of the project. The HPC Engineering department must create a skeleton BOM for all
items listed on the sales order except the drawings. Higher level assembly parts will also
be created in the complete indented BOM for the project above the level of the parts shown
on the sales order. This is done for organization (i.e., part numbers for the banks and the
project itself). These higher level parts will allow the BOM to truly reflect the actual
required quantities without requiring access to the sales order.
4.4 See figure 3 for sample project HOOO. It consists of4 different items (bundles a, b, c, d)
arranged on 5 different bays (A,B,C,D,E) in 3 different banks ("A","B","C"). Each bank
has common substructure and complete walkways. Units B and C have the same layout
(i.e., the same panels and mechanical parts) but are different only because of their bundles
(alb & bib).
4.5 For the sample project in figure 3, the BOM structure will be as shown in figure 4. Each
block represents a part number with blocks below comprising that part's BOM.
4.5.1 The project part consists ofthe different bank parts.
4.5.2 Each bank part in tum, consists ofthe units in that bank and a part (Le., assembly
60A) grouping the loose shipped components in that bank.
4.5.3 Each unit consists of part numbers for the main subassemblies (panels, mach-mts.,
bundles, etc.) ofthat unit.
4.5.4 Each main subassembly would contain lower level assemblies and parts such as
colwnns, plenum panels, bolts, etc.
4.6 For replacement bundle jobs, the bundle (HOOO-6A-3) is listed directly in the project part's
BOM. If other loose pieces are required such as shipping spares, or other loose structural
or mechanical components, the 60A is also listed in the HOOO part. The Sales Order will
list the 6A-3 and the 60A. This can change depending on the scope of the job. Production
Engineering will make the decision when to deviate.
4.7 For retube, fan sales, or other part sales, the sales order line items will depend on the scope
of that particular job. If a project number is associated with the job then a project part
number will also be created (refer to Engineering & Drafting Process For Jobs in
Standards Book I, section 2C).
4.8 Non-standard jobs may require deviation from the standard structure such that the design
philosophy of paragraph-4.2 be maintained. In these cases, Production Engineering has
authority over deviations, and will coordinate these changes with all affected departments.

ACHE PROJECT PROCESS FLOW
5.1 Project process flow steps are coordinated by the Workflow module in Visibility~ (For
more details on the Project flow process steps. refer to 6.0 and 7.0).
5.2 The project's 'Job Package' is reviewed by Drafting, Header Design. Production
Engineering. and Structural Engineering. After this review, a kick-off meeting is held with
Engineering and the Project Coordinator to layout the Visibility~ project structure. It is at
this meeting that any non-standard conditions should be discussed. if known.
5.3 The BOM Administrator creates the Skeleton BOM Request Form per the job structure as
discussed in the kick-off meeting and defmed in the 'Job Package' (refer to Skeleton BOM
Request Form in Standards Book I. section 4D.
5.4 If necessary. the drawing parts can be requested by Production Engineering and created by
the PMA in advance ofthe kick-offmeeting.
5.5 When parts are entered per Workflow, the BOM Administrator enters the skeleton BOM
into Visibility~ and has it checked by Production Engineering.
5.6 After the checked skeleton BOM has been entered, Production Engineering and Scheduling
enter routers for drafting and shop work orders. Project Coordination adds top level
assemblies to the Sales Order and work orders are then created.
5.7 Pressure and mechanical components are added to the skeleton BOM (refer to 7.2).
5.8 As drawings are detailed by Drafting, raw material part numbers are searched for in the Part
Master. New raw material part numbers are created via coordination with the PMA.
5.9 Upon completion of the 2.3.4,5,6. 7, 8. 9. corresponding 20-series drawings, Parts List,
or revisions to any ofthese, the section leader submits a copy ofthe document to the BOM
Administrator for review.
5.9.1 The BOM Administrator should check the drawings for the following details.
The bill structure is correct and easy for interpreting bill levels
i
The correct units ofmeasure are being used
The drawing numbers match the skeleton bill structure
Other problems that may cause bill errors
5.9.2 The BOM Administrator coordinates with the section leader to correct any errors
found during the review.
5.9.3 The BOM Administrator issues the drawing to the PMA for part input. The copy
ofthe drawing should include any notes from the BOM Administrator to both the
PMA and document control concerning how the bill is to be entered.
5.9.4 After part number entry (refer to Part Number Assignment in Standards Book I.
section 4A). the PMA gives the drawing to Document Control.
5.9.5 Document Control enters the BOM and submits a print out with the drawing to
the BOM Administrator.
BILLS OF MATERIALS REV. 0,12-15-98
Data Issued
By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 3A -PG. 10
5.9.6 The BOM Administrator will then check the bill input and coordinate with
Document Control to have any errors corrected.
5.9.7 The BOM Administrator submits the drawing with a signed release fonn to
Document Control to allow issuance ofthe drawing to the fabrication shop in
Beasley, Texas or an outside vendor.
5.9.8 Refer to figure 5 for a flow chart ofthese activities.

STD BOOK SECT. 3A - PC. 12
6.0 ACHE SKELETON HOM
6.1 The skeleton BOM consists ofall parts that match the scope ofwork for a project, known at
the outset ofthe project. This includes parts that will receive manufacturing and
engineering work orders linked together in a project hierarchy. It also includes other parts
known up front such as standard fan shaft, AV pipe support, nameplate, etc.
6.2 This step is the first bill input to Visibility~ and sets the project structure for the complete
BOM. The structure ofthe skeleton BOM may vary depending on the details ofthe
project, as determined at the kick-off meeting. It will follow the general guidelines
discussed for part numbers and descriptions in Bill ofMaterials Creation in Standards
Book I, section 3B.
6.3 The first step in creating a skeleton BOM is to layout the project structure on the Skeleton
BOM Request Form (refer to Skeleton BOM Request Form in Standards Book I, section
4D.
6.4 The PMA creates required parts for the assemblies and drawings listed on the Skeleton
BOM Request Form.
6.5 The BOM Administrator enters the skeleton BOM into Visibility~ per the request form, this
procedure, and the Visibility~ Engine.ering User Guide.
6.5.1 Create BOMs in the following order: any assembly with a drawing in its BOM,
6A's, 6A-3's, Unit parts, Bank parts, and Job part (refer to 6.6).
6.5.2 The indenture level on the Skeleton BOM Request Form can be used to determine
the location of each assembly and drawing in the BOM hierarchy.
6.6 Steps for entering a BOM (refer to the Visibility~ Engineering User Guide for more
information).
6.6.1 Log into the Visibility~, live database.
6.6.2 Type EN in the 'Action' field, then <ENTER>.
6.6.3 Type 10 to enter the Bills of Material menu, then <ENTER>.
6.6.4 Type 1 to select Bills of Material Maintenance, then <ENTER>.
6.6.5 In the 'Action:' field, type E to create a BOM for a part which doesn't already
have one, then <ENTER>.
6.6.6 In the 'Assembly Number:' field, either type in the part for which you are creating
a BOM or type "." to use the 'look-aside' screen to search the Part Master.
6.6.7 The BOM entry line consists ofthe following fields arranged in two lines as
shown:
Item, Component, Description, Level, Unit ofMeasure (UoM), Qty Per, Spares
Revised, Drawing Ref, Kit, Ph, Fx, Last Chg, Operation, Text
6.6.7.1 Item: a numeric sequential value which determines the order in which
the BOM components are displayed when printed or viewed on-line.

When entering, start with 10 and increment by 10. The 7A assembly
in the 6A-3 BOM should use 500 and al16A-3 components detailed on
the 7A drawing should follow, incrementing by 10. The 7A bolts
should start with number 1000.
6.6.7.2 Component: the part number for the components in the BOM. Enter
the part number or type to use the look-aside screen.
n.n
6.6.7.3 Description, Level, UoM: these fields are automatically filled-in once
the part number is entered. Check that the description agrees with the
part you thought you were entering. Level is NOT the same as
indenture level (refer to 3.2.5 and 6.9.7) in the indented BOM print­
out.
6.6.7.4 Qty Per: enter the amount ofthat component required to build one of
the part shown in the 'Assembly Number:' field. Quantity is in terms
ofthe UoM. Round all decimals to 3 digits.
6.6.7.5 Spares: press <ENTER> to use the default of zero.
6.6.7.6 Revised: this field is automatically left blank. the first time a BOM is
created. Thereafter, this field will show the date this item was added
to the BOM or last revised.
6.6.7.7 Drawing Ref, Kit: press <ENTER> in each ofthese fields to use the
defaults.
6.6.7.8 Ph: refers to the Phantom flag. Press <ENTER> to use the default
value (refer to 6.8 for phantom flag settings).
6.6.7.9 Fx: press <ENTER> in this field, unless the part entered is a drawing
or the testing spares assembly, in which case type Y, then <ENTER>.
This prevents the BOM quantity from 'rolling-up' with multiple
assemblies. Occasionally other parts will be 'fixed'. Production
Engineering will make that decision.
6.6.7.10 Last Chg, Operation, Text: press <ENTER> in these fields to use the
defaults.
6.6.8 After all items have been entered, type II, then <ENTER> in the next 'Item' field
to return to the 'Action:' field.
6.6.9 Type US, then <ENTER> to update the information and stay in this screen.
6.6.10 Ifmore than 7 components are used in the BOM, enter the first 7 parts per steps
6.6.1 through 6.6.9. From the 'Action:' field, type A and continue entering more
components per steps 6.6.5 through 6.6.10 until all components have been entered
(pay attention to the item numbers and make sure they are sequential and none are
duplicated).
6.7 Steps for editing an existing BOM.
6.7.1 From the 'Action:' field type F, then <ENTER>.

6.7.2 Type the part number whose BOM you want to edit, then <ENTER> twice. Press
<ENTER> to scroll through the BOM until you locate the component you wish to
change or delete. Ifadding a component, scroll through the list to locate the place
where you wish to insert the part. Note the item number range in which the added
component should fall, then scroll to find the last component in the BOM.
6.7.3 To delete a component, type D-x in the 'Action:' field, then <ENTER>. This will
delete line x (do not confuse line number with item number). The line number
can only be 1 through 7 and corresponds to the 7 components that can be shown
on a screen. Type D-xly to delete lines x through y. Type US, then <ENTER>.
6.7.4 To modify a component, type the line number of the component in the 'Action:'
field, then <ENTER>. This will move the cursor to the 'Item' field on that line.
Press <ENTER> in fields you do not want to change. Type new values, then
<ENTER> to replace those you do want to change. Continue this until the cursor
returns to the 'Action:' field. Type US, then <ENTER>.
6.7.5 To modify more than one line, type xly in the 'Action:' field, then <ENTER> to
edit lines x through y (refer to 6.7.4).
6.7.6 To add a component, type A in the 'Action:' field, then <ENTER>. Be sure to
determine the correct item number (refer to 6.7.2). Use steps 6.6.5 through 6.6.10
to add new components.
6.8 The Phantom flag should be set to N for any ofthe following conditions. If none of these
conditions apply set it to Y.
6.8.1 All purchased parts.
6.8.2 All drawing parts numbers.
6.8.3 All main assemblies listed below.
HOOO HOOO-29A Shafts
HOOO-iiA HOOO-6A-3 AV Pipe Supports

("B" and "C", etc., assemblies also apply, i.e., "HOOO-A" also represents
"HOOO-B/C/O...)
6.8.4 All stocked standard parts. HPC stocked standard parts are listed below.

6.9 Printing the BOM:
6.9.1 After the Skeleton BOM is completed by the BOM Administrator, the indented
BOM for the highest level part (usually the job part) should be printed.
6.9.2 From the Bills of Material menu, type 9, then <ENTER>. In the 'Action:' field,
type E, then <ENTER>.
6.9.3 In the 'Type' field, type E for an indented BOM, J for a single-level BOM, H for
a costed indented BOM, or ?? to see the menu ofother available reports (use up
and down arrows to scroll through the options), then <ENTER>.
6.9.4 In the 'Part Number' field, type the part number associated with the BOM that is
to be printed, then <ENTER>.
6.9.5 In the 'Requester' field, type your initials, then <ENTER>.
6.9.6 If the cursor stops in the 'Quantity' field, type the quantity ofthat part's BOM
you are concerned with, then <ENTER>. Otherwise the cursor should move to
the 'Low-LvI' field. Proceed to 6.9.7.
6.9.7 Type the lowest level of parts you want to print. This level refers to the 'Level' of
a part that is determined by the system. Do no confuse this level with the
'Indenture Level' (refer to 3.2.5). This level is the lowest level that that part is
used anywhere in bills. If a component has a level of 04 and it is used on a bill
whose part is a level 05, the component's level will be changed to 06. Purchased
parts are almost always level 99. If you want all parts to be printed, press
<ENTER> in this field to use the default of 99.
6.9.8 In the 'Txt' field, type Y if you want BOM text to print or N if you don't want
BOM text to print, then <ENTER>.
6.9.9 The cursor should now be in the 'Type' field on the next line. You can now
request other reports by repeating steps 6.9.3 through 6.9.9 until all reports have
been requested. If you use up all 18 lines, the cursor will automatically return to
the 'Action:' field. If not, type II, then <ENTER>. Type DR, then <ENTER> to
save the information and exit the screen.
6.9.10 In the Bills of Material menu, press the <ESC> key to return to the Engineering
menu.

6.9.11 Type RP, then <ENTER> to go to the Reports & Procedures menu.

to the report just requested. Type 16 for an indented BOM, 7 for a single-level
BOM, 19 for a costed indented BOM, etc. Then press <ENTER>.
6.9.13 In the Parameter Entry screen, enter the your initials in the 'Print Reports
Requested By:' field, then <ENTER>.
6.9.14 Type GO in the 'Action:' field, then <ENTER>.

<ENTER> to display the output to your computer monitor. Ifyou typed 1/2 in
step 6.9.15, you will first need to type 0, then <ENTER> before proceeding to
field 2.
6.9.17 In the 'Action:' field, type, then <ENTER>.
6.9.18 Press <ENTER>. If you have different types ofreports to print and you did not
select'All Bill ofMaterial Reports' in step 6.9.12, you will have to repeat steps
6.9.11 through 6.9.18 until all reports have been printed.
6.9.19 Refer to the Visibility~ Engineering User Guide for more information on
requesting reports.
7.0 ACHE FULL HOM
7.1 After the skeleton BOM has been entered and engineering and manufacturing work orders
have been created, the main assemblies ofthe skeleton BOM will be completed with all
components (refer to Bill ofMaterials Creation in Standards Book I, section 3B). Ifa
skeleton level assembly does not exist, consult the BOM Administrator immediately.
7.2 The Header Designer and Drafting will add pressure and mechanical components to the
skeleton BOM.
7.2.1 The Header Designer creates the detailed BOM for pressure retaining parts while
Drafting creates the detailed BOM for mechanical parts.
7.2.2 All ofthese bills are entered into temporary assembly bills.
7.2.3 A part number request form must be sent to the PMA prior to bill entry ifa part
number does not already exist in the Part Master when the temporary bill is being
generated.
7.2.4 These temporary bills are checked by the appropriate person then the bills are
copied to the correct assembly.
7.2.5 The temporary bills are then deleted.

7.2.6 The BOM Administrator does a cursory check that the copy was perfonned

7.3 Searching for a part number in Visibility~ (refer to the Visibility~ General Inquiry User
Guide for more infonnation).
7.3.1 Log into the Visibility~ live database.
7.3.2 Type IQ, then <ENTER>.
7.3.3 Type 1, then <ENTER> to select by part number.
7.3.4 In the 'Part Number:' field, type *, then <ENTER> to use the 'look-aside' screen.
Proceed to step 7.3.5 if you are searching for a string ofcharacaters at the
beginning ofthe part number or description. Ifyou are searching for a string of
characters in the middle of the description or part number, skip to step 7.3.1 O.
7.3.5 Type the part number string, then <ENTER> or <ENTER>, the description string
, then <ENTER> again.
7.3.6 From the 'Select:' field, press <ENTER> to scroll through the list ofparts until
you find a part that might match the one for which your are searching.
7.3.7 In the 'Select:' field, type the line number that corresponds to the part you think
might be correct, then <ENTER>. Ifno part matches, you will need to make a
request for a new part (refer to Part Number Assignment in Standards Book I,
section 4A).
7.3.8 From the 'Action:' field in the Parts Master Inquiry screen, type 6, then
<ENTER>.
7.3.9 View the complete description. If it does not match the part you are attempting to
use you will need to make a request for a new part (refer to Part Number
Assignment in Standards Book I, section 4A).
7.3.10 Press the <ESC> key.
7.3.11 Type S, then <ENTER>.
7.3.12 Press <ENTER> three times. This will return the cursor to the 'Select: field.
7.3.13 Type 1, then <ENTER>.
7.3.14 If you wish to search for a string in the part number, type the following string then
<ENTER>. If you do not wish to search on the part number then press
<ENTER>.
7.3.14.1 %@??????@ to search for the string "??????" (i.e., type %@7K4@ to
find all parts with "7K4" anywhere in the part number, revision or
description)
7.3.15 If you wish to search for a string in the revision column, then type the string in
7.3.14.1, then <ENTER>. Ifnot,just press <ENTER>.
