7.4 Create the detail drawings then add the parts from the drawings to the appropriate skeleton
bills (refer to 6.6 and 6.7).
7.4.1 As drawings are detailed and checked, but before releasing to the BaM
Administrator for review, search the Part Master for all raw material required
(refer to7.3).
7.4.2 Enter existing raw material part numbers on the drawings per the instructions for
that particular series ofdrawing.
7.4.3 All structural (i.e., non-header) plate will be called from the "RNDM" part
number for the appropriate thickness, with a UoM of square feet. Do not use parts
with actual plate dimensions (L x W).
7.4.4 The part number for standard structural bolts includes one nut. Washers,
however, are not included and will need to be listed separately.
7.4.5 If the raw material does not exist in the Part Master, coordinate with the PMA to
create the raw material part number (refer to Part Number Assignment in
Standards Book I, section 4A).
7.4.6 After the new part number has been added to the Part Master, you can use it on
the drawing.
7.4.7 Follow steps in paragraph 5.9 to enter ETa parts and all bills.

S'I'D BOOR HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT 3B -PG.l
BILL OF MATERIALS CREATION
1.0 PURPOSE & INTRODUCTION
1.1 This procedure explains how the complete bill ofmaterials for an ACHE is structured.
1.2 It defines how to number and describe the skeleton level parts.
1.3 Part numbers will also be created and inserted into the indented BOM that represent work
performed in the Engineering department. These parts are not addressed in this document.
Refer to Engineering Part Number Management in Engineering Standards Book I, section
3C for information on how to handle these parts.
1.4 Occasionally, there will be projects that do not fit this standard bill format. When these
situations occur, Production Engineering will determine the bill and description formats.
1.5 In the following paragraphs HOOO is used as a generic project number and part numbers
contain the variable X in italic font. The actual project number should be used in place of
HOOO. A letter that uniquely identifies a particular assembly will replace the variable X.
This letter is not significant and does not necessarily correspond to any other assembly in
the indented BOM.
1.6 The Skeleton BOM - At the outset ofa project, an indented BOM, outlining the scope of
the project, is generated. This BOM is referred to as the Skeleton BOM. It consists only of
high level assemblies and is created so that work orders can be generated and scheduled
long before the drawings that detail the assemblies are created.
1.7 Completed BOM
1.7.1 After the assembly drawings are completed, the rest ofthe BOM is entered into
the various assemblies ofthe skeleton BOM. The different types ofparts that can
be added to the BOM at this point are purchased, standard, and ETO.
1.7.2 The Standards Department determines part numbers for Standard Parts.
1.7.3 Purchased parts are 5-digit, numeric part numbers determined by the PMA.
1.7.4 ETO part numbers are always in the form ofProject-Drawing-Piece mark. Refer
to ETO Descriptionsfor Parts and Assemblies, Standards Book I, section 4B for
description formats ofthese parts.
Example: HOOO-7X-l or HOOO-5X-A
BILL OF MATERIALS CREATION REV. 3, 7-11-2000

STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT 3B -,G.3
3.0 SKELETON BOM PART NUMBERS
3.1 Project HOOO
A part that is created for each project and is the highest level in the skeleton BOM.
3.2 Banks HOOO-llX
A part number will be created for each unique bank in a project.
3.3 Units HOOO-X
A part number will be created for each unique ACHE unit.
3.4 Base Units (Bays) HOOO-345X
This assembly consists ofthe plenum and machinery mount and exist only in forced draft
units. A part number is created to represent each unique base unit.
3.5 Plenum Panels HOOO-3X
This is a collection of sheet metal components in the plenum. A part number will be
created for each unique set ofplenum panels.
3.6 Plenum Structure HOOO-5X
This is a collection of all structural members in the plenum. A part number will be created
for each unique set ofplenum structure.
3.7 Machinery Mounts HOOO-4X-1
This is a welded assembly to which the mechanical components and motor mount are
attached. A part number will be created for each unique machinery mount assembly.
3.8 Machinery Mount Assemblies HOOO-4X
This is a collection ofmachinery mounting hardware that includes the machinery mount,
fan mount, and removable tie rod tube assembly (if required) and can be found only on
induced draft units. A part number will be created for each unique set ofmachinery
mounting hardware.
3.9 Hoods HOOO-3X
This is an assembly ofpanels that is found only on induced draft units. It sits on top ofthe
unit and there is typically one hood per fan. Ifthe hoods for two fans share a wall, then
there is only one hood for both fans. A part number will be created to represent each
unique hood.
3.10 Hood Walkway Supports HOOO-5X
This is a collection of all support brackets for hood walkways on a give unit. A part
number will be created of each unique set ofsupport brackets.
3.11 Bundles HOOO-6X-3
This is the main assembly on an ACHE where the heat transfer takes place. It consists of
the header boxes, tubes, and a supporting frame. A part number will be created for each
unique bundle.
3.12 Headers HOOO-6X
This is a collection ofheader boxes for a given bundle. A part number will be created for
each unique bundle.
BILL OF MATERIALS CREATION REV. 3, 7-11-2000

S'I'DBOOK I HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SEC'I'3B-PG.4
3.13 Nozzles HOOO-6X-2
This is a collection ofnozzle parts (flanges, transitions, thredolets, etc.) for a given bundle.
A part number will be created for each unique bundle. This assembly is required only on
plug and coverplate headers.
3.14 Tubes HOOO-6X-4Y
This can be either a bare tube or one with fins. A part number will be created for each
unique tube in each unique bundle. The X should always correspond with the bundle. The
Y is included only iftheir all multiple tube sizes within the bundle. Together, X and Y (if
required) will uniquely identify a tube.
Tubes on Pipe & V-Bend bundles and Serpentine coils may also include a 180-degree
return welded to one end. These bundles may also have a tube which is has no fins and is
bent into a 180-degree return. In all cases each unique tube assembly will receive a part
number.
3.15 Bundle Frame HOOO-7X
This is a collection of frame components that are fabricated under a single work order. A
part number will be created for each unique bundle.
3.16 Retaining Air Seal Assembly HOOO-7X-AS
This is a collection of side air seals that are attached to the bundle frame side channels and
their clips. A part number will be created for each unique bundle that has these seals.
3.17 Louvers (bundle exhaust) HOOO-9X
This is the set oflouvers (with and without bug screens) that are attached to the top ofthe
bundle. A part number will be created for each unique set of louvers.
3.18 Bug Screens (in bundles) HOOO-9X
This is the set ofbugscreens that are either below or in the bundle. They are typically shop­
installed. A part number will be created for each unique set ofbug screens.
3.19 Shafts HOOO-IOYA-X
The Y is either 1 for induced draft or 2 for forced draft. Typically, this part is not required
on forced draft units since those shafts have been standardized. The X is an integer (not a
letter) that uniquely identifies a shaft. A part number will be created for each unique ETO
shaft.
At the outset ofa project, only HOOO-101A-l or HOOO-I02A-l will be created. This part
number will be used for every shaft on the project and will be replaced with new part
numbers when necessary after the shaft drawing(s) have been completed.
3.20 Mechanical Items HOOO-I2X
This is a collection of equipment for a given fan, including (if required): mechanical
components, guards, fan-ring strut, AV support, and AV clip. There is one set of
equipment for each fan. A part number will be created for each different collection of
components.
3.21 Loose Field Items HOOO-60X
This is a collection of assemblies and miscellaneous parts that will ship to the field loose.
These parts will be separated into groups by bank and shipment. A part number is created
for each unique group ofparts.
3.22 Doors HOOO-2X

S'I'DBOOR HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SEC'f3B-PG.S
This is a collection of equipment that makes up doors on winterized banks. Doors in bug
screens are grouped with the bug screens and panels in hoods are considered panels and not
doors. These parts will be separated into groups by bank and shipment. A part number
will be created for each unique group ofparts.
3.23 Field Panels HOOO-23X
This is a collection ofpanels that are typically installed in the field. They can include air
seals, wind skirts, winterization panels, or other miscellaneous panels. These panels will be
separated into groups by bank, type (air seals, wind skirts, etc.), and shipment. A part
number will be created for each unique group ofparts.
3.24 Bank Structure HOOO-25X
This is a collection ofstructural members (e.g., columns, beams, bracing, brackets, etc.)
that support the units, walkways, winterization, and other bank components. These parts
will be separated into groups by bank and shipment. A part number will be created for
each unique group ofparts.
3.25 Walkways HOOO-28X
This is a collection ofwalkway assemblies (platforms, ladders, handrails, etc.) for
mechanical, header, hood, and side access walkways. These assemblies are separated into
groups by bank and shipment. A part number will be created for each unique group of
assemblies.
3.26 Louvers (field installed) HOOO-29X
This is a collection of louvers that are typically installed in the field. This includes intake
louvers, re-circulation louvers, etc. These parts will be separated into groups by bank and
shipment. A part number will be created for unique group ofparts.
3.27 Bug Screens (field installed) HOOO-29X
This is a collection ofbug screens that are typically installed in the field. The majority of
these will be bug screens around the perimeter ofthe bank. These parts will be separated
into groups by bank and shipment. A part number will be created for each unique group of
parts.
3.28 Field Bolts HOOO-30X
This is a collection of all fasteners required to perform all assembly in the field. These
fasteners will be separated into groups by bank and shipment. A part number will be
created for each unique group offasteners.

table 3. Tubes not shown will not require the TOOLING part.

grouped as mentioned above. These bills will follow a similar format

6.3 Bill ofMaterials
6.3.1 The BaM for fan assemblies will be created and maintained by the HPC Fan
Engineering Department.
6.3.2 The BaM for all ACHE fan assemblies will consist of the hub and blades. AV
fans will also include a coupling, valve positioner, filter regulator, and other AV
hardware. 'AC?F' hubs will not include the coupling.
6.3.3 Components that are NOT included in this assembly are the bushing (for non­
tapered shafts), retainer plate assembly (for tapered shafts), and inlet bell sets.
These are added to the HOOO-I2XBOM.
6.3.4 Fans which are used on non-HPC ACHE applications are called out as Sales
Order line items by the Fan Sales Department. These fans use Features & Options
to select special parameters in the hubs, spools, or bushings; therefore the BOMs
for these fans do not have these components. These BOMs consist only ofblades,
seal discs, and seal disc hardware.
6.3.5 All fans will consist ofsomeorall ofthe following components: fan blades, seal
discs, seal disc hardware, hubs
6.3.6 When required, a modified seal disc is a manufactured part with the standard seal
disc in its BaM.
6.3.7 Seal disc hardware - Some seal discs include the mounting hardware as part of the
purchased part. For discs which do not, the hardware is included in a "HWKIT"
BaM. This kit part is included in the fan BaM.
6.3.8 Fan hubs are either AP or AV. These assemblies include (as required): the hub
body, spool, blade clamps, couplings, hardware, etc.
6.3.8.1 AP hubs are either cast or plate. The cast hub consists ofthe finished
hub (made from the purchased hub casting and the machining part) and
the blade retainer rings. The plate hub consists ofthe top and bottom
plates, spool, stop plate, blade clamps, blade arms (ifrequired), and
hardware. These hubs have full BOMs for AC fans, but for other fans,
the hub is compiled by Features & Options to handle parameters such
as coal tar coating, alloy hardware, special bores, etc.
6.3.8.2 AV hubs consist of the hub body, coupling, and all components in the
AV adjustment mechanism. This will include different range springs
for different blade angles or fan sizes.
6.4 New Fans
6.4.1 Fan Engineering will coordinate with the PMA to create new fans or revise
existing ones. They will do so per the structure of similarly configured fans, such
that the assembly hierarchy is maintained.

APPENDIX A: AMENDMENTS, revision 3.0
This appendix will list those changes to this procedure that occur between major revisions.
Therefore, this section may carry a different revision mark than the document itself. The
revision number for this appendix will start with the number ofthe document followed by a
decimal then the revision ofthe appendix. Upon receipt ofthis appendix, you should mark up
the main portion ofthe document with the corrections below so that you do not have to
constantly refer here for the most recent procedures.
This appendix is laid out with four columns. The first column gives the paragraph that is
being replaced, deleted, or added to the procedure. The second column describes how the
paragraph is being changed (R = replacing, A = adding, D = deleting). The third column
gives the revision number ofthe change. This column will help to track changes when a
paragraph has been revised more than once. The fourth column is the new or replaced
paragraph. If a paragraph has been deleted from the procedure, this fourth column will be
blank. If a paragraph has been deleted, the other paragraphs will NOT be renumbered. The
renumbering will take place on the next major revision to the entire document.
The most recent revisions will be in bold face type.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 3C -PG. 1
ENGINEERING - DRAWING PART NUMBER MANAGEMENT
1.0 PURPOSE & INTRODUCTION
1.1 Identify which drawing part numbers will be created and in which bills these part numbers
will reside.
1.2 Establish a description structure for each drawing part number.
1.3 Define how and when work orders for these part numbers will be created.
1.4 Establish the hierarchy of these work orders and the structure of their routers.
1.5 Define the meaning of operations.
1.6 Define time charging for work and move-tickets performed in HPC drafting and
engineering departments. Outline when move-tickets are performed and by whom, but not
how. Refer to Time & Attendance and Move Tickets and Salaried Timesheet Entry in
Standards Book I, sections 2A and 2B, respectively, for how to perform time charges and
move tickets.
1.7 This document requires prior knowledge of each drawing and other documents created and
maintained by the Engineering department.
1.8 Throughout this document the generic term #000 is used and is meant to refer to the
alphanumeric job number, with # representing the alphabet, e. g, job number HOOO, 1000,
and so on. Also throughout this document, D attached to the job number, i.e., D#OOO, is
meant to refer to the drawing part numbers, e.g. DHOOO-OA, DJOOO-OA, and so on.
1.9 The sections of this document only cover normal situations. Production Engineering may
deviate from this procedure taking into account the following considerations:
Drafting and/or Engineering is notified of the changes.
The two main purposes ofwork orders are to schedule engineering activities and to collect
and organize labor costs.
If a change becomes permanent, this procedure should be updated as soon as possible.
1.10 Appendix notations are reference with superscript numbers, e.g., 01501 Dwg to ... and
, 3,
so on.
ENGINEERING DRAWING PART NUMBER MANAGEMENT REV. 7, 03-22-02

3.0 DRAWING PART NUMBERS
3.1 Unit Subassemblies Drawings
3.1.1 Drawing Part Number is D#OOO-YX
Y is the series (as listed in table 1)
X is the letter ofthe assembly (refer to Bill of Material Creation in Standards
Book I, section 3B)
SERIES ASSEMBLY
3 Plenums and Hoods
4 Machinery Mounts
5 Shop-Assembled Structural
6 Headers
7 Bundle Frames (process and steam coil)
8 Shop-Assembled Walkways
9 Shop-Assembled Louvers
Table 1: Assemblies that are typically Shop-Assembled
3.1.2 Part Number Scope:
a. Creation of all drawings in a series.
b. Creation of the series sheets associated with these drawings.
c. Placement of piece marks on the appropriate assembly drawing.
3.1.3 Example 1
Assembly, part number: #OOO-4A
machinery mount
Drawings required to detail: #OOO-4A
Drawing part number: D#OOO-4A
time for drawing, series sheet, and adding piece marks to the unit assembly
drawing.
3.1.4 Example 2
Assembly, part number: #OOO-7B
side channels, cross members, header pads, etc. that make up the tube
bundle frame.
Drawings required to detail: #OOO-7B, #OOO-7B 1
Drawing part number: D#OOO-7B
time for drawings, the series sheet(s), and adding piece marks to the unit
assembly drawing.

3.14 Finite Element Analysis (FEA)
3.14.1 A part number is created in the form ofD#OOO-FEAX; where X equals the
drawings, for example, 6A (FEAA), 6B (FEAB), and so on.
3.14.2 The steps required to complete the FEA are covered in the scope for the header
design part numbers (D#000-H6X) and D#OOO-JOB.
3.14.3 Refer to section 10 (Operation Scope of Work) of this document for instructions on
which steps go with which part numbers.
3.15 Other part numbers and/or routing operations will be created for engineering activities on a
case-by-case basis (determined by Production Engineering and the Drafting Manager) when a
situation does not fit the standard. The following are some examples of when this would
occur.
a. Non-ACHE jobs such as the Split-Flo® and various Therm-Flo® products.
b. ACHE projects with unusual requirements.
3.16 The Parts Master Administrator (PMA) should use the following default values for each
drawing part number.

a. Make/Buy Code = M
b. Planner Code = 30
c. Unit of Measure = DW
d. Commodity Code = EDET

4.0 BOM PLACEMENT OF DRAWING PART NUMBERS
4.1 The following rules apply when entering Drawing part numbers into a BaM.
4.1.1 The 'Fix' flag is set to 'Y'.
4.1.2 The quantity is 1.
4.1.3 The part number is the first item in the bill. However, it should be the last item in
the bill under these circumstances:
a. It represents a set of drawings sent to the customer at the start of a project.
b. It is placed on the BaM of #000.
c. It represents header design engineering.
4.2 A drawing part number, listed in table 1 or 2, that represents a drawing of an assembly is
placed in the BaM for that assembly.
4.3 D#000-3A hood drawing part number is placed in the BaM of the first hood assembly
scheduled to be fabricated.
4.3.1 When the skeleton bill is created, it is placed in #000-3A.
4.3.2 After fabrication work orders are scheduled, it is moved to the correct BaM.
4.3.3 Example:
a. A job requires: #000-3A, #000-3B, #000-3C
b. D#000-3A is placed in the #000-3A BaM when the skeleton bill is created.
c. The order of fabrication is: #000-3C, #000-3A, #000-3B
d. Move D#000-3A to #000-3C.
4.4 D#OOO-lOXS is placed in the BaM ofthe first ACHE in bank X scheduled to be fabricated.
4.4.1 When the skeleton bill is created, it is placed in the BaM of the first ACHE,
alphabetically, in the bank.
4.4.2 After fabrication work orders are scheduled, it is moved to the correct BaM.

7.0 EXPLANATION OF DESCRIPTIONS
7.1 #-1 qty of units in the bank; from 01 to 99 units.
7.2 #-2 qty of different items in the bank, from 01 to 99 items.
7.3 #-3 qty of fans on the unit.
7.4 #-4 qty of different hood designs used on the project; from 01 to 99 designs.
7.5 #-5 qty of shaft designs in the project; from 01 to 99 designs.
7.6 #-6 qty of banks in the project; from 01 to 99 banks.
7.7 3-Assy PLENUM or HOOD,NTD (non-standard hood designs).
7.8 Draft FD for forced draft unit, ND for induced draft unit, NA for natural draft unit.
7.9 Hdr HDR for process header only.
7.10 UoM S for standard units on drawings, M if metric units are required.
7.11 NP include NP only if no proposal header design was created.
7.12 Item customer item number(s).
7.13 6-Type header type; complete list of header types is located in Bill ofMaterial Creation,
Standard Book I, section 3B (examples: PLG for plug and THC for thru-bolt
confined coverplate)
7.14 7-Type TH for process bundles or SC for steam coils.
7.15 WW-Design HPC if a standard Hudson design, NON if another design.
7.16 Ifthe drive is a gear drive, add ,GEAR to the end of the 0#000-4 and 0#000-5 descriptions.
7.17 II-Type is per the following options. Add required option(s) (if any) in the order listed;
separate by commas.
BUG Bug screens around all or part ofthe bank's perimeter
WIN Wind skirts around all or part ofthe bank's perimeter
BUGIWIN Bug screens and wind skirts around part ofthe bank's perimeter
WNT winterization around all or part of the bank's perimeter
STK exhaust stack on top of unit
7.18 5-Type is per the following options:
STD structural components are predominantly standard
NTD structural components are predominantly non-standard
JHN Johnson design (rotated stub columns)
7.19 7-Type2 is per the following options. Add all that apply (if any) in the order listed, separated
by commas, to the end ofthe 0#000-7 description.
ST shaft-thru bundle
SL sloped tubes (l or more rows)
TO flanges are toed out

8.0 WORK ORDERS
8.1 A work order identifies a task, such as the creation of a drawing or set of drawings.
8.2 A work order will be created for each and every drawing part number created.
8.3 Production Planning and Scheduling personnel (PP&S) create most ofthese work orders
when project work orders are created.
8.4 The following work orders are created by Production Engineering:
8.4.1 D#OOO-JOB work order is created immediately after the kickoff meeting
8.4.2 D#OOO-RT work order is created immediately after the kickoff meeting (if
required)
8.4.3 D#000-H6X work orders are created immediately after the kickoff meeting
8.4.4 Work orders for drawings sent to the customer at the start of a project. These
orders will be created soon after the kickoff meeting.
8.4.5 Work orders for some drawings nonnally created by PP&S.
a. Done on fast-track projects to expedite detailing when PP&S can't create orders
fast enough.
b. After PP&S creates work orders for the project, Production Engineering must
delete duplicated orders created by PP&S and link the expedited orders to the
correct fabricated work order.
8.4.6 Other work orders as required (including work orders for non-ACHE projects).
8.5 When PP&S reschedules the fabrication schedule for a project, the linked drawing work
orders are also rescheduled. However, the completion date for drawing Work Orders may
remain as is and therefore may fall after the Shop Kitup date. In these situations, 'HD'
should be added to line 10 in the Work Order Maintenance screen of Visibility. This will be
used by PP&S's scheduling program to 'hold' the schedule dates for the drafting work order.
9.0 DRAFTINGIENGINEERING ROUTERS FOR DRAWING PART NUMBERS
9.1 An operation is a step required to completing a task. A router is a sequence ofoperations
required to complete a work order.

9.2 The scope of work for an operation is dependent upon the operation description. An attempt
is made to keep operation numbers consistent for each operation description. However,
sometimes this can not be done. Care should be taken to follow the operation description.
9.3 Two types of routers exist:
a. DraftinglEngineering Router: is associated with a part number and is used as the
default router when work orders are created.
b. Shop Floor Router: is associated with a work order. It is created by attaching the
DraftinglEngineering Router to a work order and can be
manipulated separately from the DraftinglEngineering Router.
9A Drafting routings are inputted for all drafting Work Orders.
9.5 Appendix A contains tables listing the complete routers used on engineering work orders.
9.5.1 Documents created by HPM and other vendors are included.
9.5.2 Each table lists (from left to right) the following information:
a. Operation number
b. Description of the operation.
c. Personnel responsible for performing the move ticket on that operation.
d. When the move ticket is to be performed.
10.0 OPERATION SCOPE OF WORK
10.1 LAYOUT
a. This covers the creation ofinformal layouts, ifrequired, that facilitate the detailing ofthe
assembly components.
b. This includes the checking and scrubbing ofthose layouts.
10.2 DETAIL
a. The Detailer creates the first draft of the document(s).
b. This draft can be done using any tool (Pro-Engineer®, AutoCAD®, etc.). The medium is
identified in the 'Tools' field on the Visibility router.
10.3 CHECK
The checker checks the first draft of the document(s).
lOA SCRUB
a. The detailer reviews the checker's comments and scrubs the drawing as required until
complete.
b. The detailer creates the series sheet(s) if necessary.
c. The detailer places piece marks on the unit assembly drawing(s) if necessary.
10.5 CHECK SCRUB
ENGINEERING DRAWING PART NUMBER MANAGEMENT REV. 7, 03-22-02

By: Barnes, Carbrey

The checker rechecks the document(s) after scrubbing until complete.
10.6 SIGN DRAWING
Engineer reviews the document(s) and signs it.
10.7 ISSUE
10.7.1 If revision 0 is being issued to the shop:
a. Input of part numbers and bills into Visibility if necessary.
b. Check of inputs.
c. Issue document(s) to shop.
10.7.2 If revision 0 is being issued only to the customer:
a. May include the input of part numbers and bills into Visibility.
b. Issue document(s) to customer.
10.7.3 Unit Assembly Drawing (D#000-10XS)
Completion ofthe blank drawing(s) without piece marks.
10.8 KITTING
10.8.1 If revision 0 is being issued to the shop:
a. Period from issuance of document to start of fabrication
b. PP&S uses this to pad the schedule for allowance ofmaterial procurement and
the preparation of the work order package.
10.8.2 If revision 0 was issued only to the customer and is now being issued to the shop:
a. Input of part numbers and bills into Visibility, if necessary.
b. Check of input.
c. Issue document(s) to shop.
10.8.3 Unit Assembly Drawing (D#000-10XS)
a. Issuance of drawing(s) with piece marks.
b. Adding piece marks is not covered on this work order.
10.9 HDR SPEC REVIEW
a. If on the header design work order, Header Designer reviews customer specifications, the
Fin-Fan Specification Sheet (FFSS), and project requirements
®
b. If on the work order for D#OOO-JOB, the header design checker reviews customer
specifications, the FFSS, and project requirements.
10.1 0 ANSWER QUESTIONS
a. Header Designer formulates questions for the project coordinator and customer.
b. Header Designer gets a satisfactory answer.
10.11 DESIGN

10.12 CHECK DESIGN

Header-design Checker rechecks the design after scrubbing until complete.
10.15 REVISION -RT
All revisions for retube documents after they have been issued.
10.16 MISC - RT
Miscellaneous work for retube portion of a project.
10.17 CLOSEOUT ENG/DRAFT
This operation is a control step that allows Production Engineering to leave the work order
open until shipping, protecting against automatic closing by APRON (Advance Production
Receipt On Notice).
10.18 FEA REPORTS,#-ITEM
a. Header Designer sets up a model that will be used to perform the FEA.
b. This includes all steps required to prepare the program for running and tweaking model
until the program runs successfully.
a. Header Designer writes up the reports for the FEA for all items on a project.
b. This step should be copied to the work order for D#OOO-FEAX as operation 5000.
c. # is replaced with the number of items requiring an FEA for a given project.
10.19 CHECK FEA
a. Header-design Checker checks the report given by Header Designer.
b. This step should be copied to the work order for D#OOO-FEAX as operation 5100.
10.20 ADMINISTRATIVE
This operation covers all time for section leaders spent on a project.
10.21 STRUCTURAL ENG
a. Structural Engineer reviews customer specifications, the FFSS, and project requirements.
b. Engineer develops the Reaction Chart (includes check and scrub if necessary).
c. Engineer develops structural design, i.e., Drafting Checklist and any other miscellaneous
documents (includes check and scrub if necessary).

a. Time for correcting a document or set ofdocuments as the result of a customer change.

for D#OOO-JOB.

done at the discretion ofthe Drafting Supervisor and Production Engineering.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 3C - PC. 18
10.27 CHECK OTHER DOC'S
Time for Drafting Checker to check and re-check miscellaneous documents not covered
elsewhere.
10.28 SCHEM, #-BNDL
a. Header Designer creates and scrubs the plate schematics for non-stocked plate
specifications.
b. # is replaced with the actual number of bundles requiring plate schematics.
10.29 SCHEM-CHECK, #- BNDL
a. Header-design Checker checks and rechecks the plate schematics.
b. # is replaced with the actual number ofbundles requiring plate schematics.
10.30 BOM, #-ITEM
a. Header Designer determines what part numbers are required to meet the design
requirements.
b. If necessary, temporary bills are entered in Visibility for the bundle, header, nozzle, and
fin-tube assemblies.
c. If necessary, spare parts are added to the appropriate Visibility bill.
d. # is replaced with the actual number of items in a job requiring bills.
10.31 BOM-CHECK, #-ITEM
a. Header-design Checker reviews the part numbers selected by the header designer.
b. Header-design Checker reviews any temporary bills created and spare parts added to
actual bills.
c. # is replaced with the actual number of items in a job requiring bills.
10.32 BOM-SCRUB, #-ITEM
a. Header Designer scrubs and Header-design Checker rechecks the temporary bills and the
spare parts bills until complete.
b. Header Designer forwards list of correct part numbers to Document control for Visibility
bill entry.
c. If necessary, Header Designer copies the temporary bills to actual ones.
d. # is replaced with the actual number of items in a job requiring bills.
11.0 REVISIONS
11.1 There are many different types of revisions that can be handled in a number of ways. The
manner in which a particular revision is handled directly affects how time charges and move
tickets are done. The following are guidelines for how to handle revisions. Production
Engineering and Drafting Supervisor will make the final decision on a case-by-case basis.
11.2 In these instructions, the cause of the revision does not matter. These instructions will hold
whether the revision is a customer revision or a detailing error.

11.3 Types of revisions
a. Revisions to assemblies before detailing starts
b. Design change before initial issue
c. Changes after drawing has been issued
d. Approval drawing mark-ups

start the drawing, charging time and doing move tickets normally, with the latest design.
11.5 Refer to the chapter on 'Operation Scope of Work' above for where to charge time for
revisions that occur before and after the first issue (including approval mark-ups).
11.6 When a revision is required, Production Engineering and Drafting Supervisor should be
notified. They should be made aware of the exact nature and scope of the change.

4.0 ENGINEERING ROUTERS FOR ENGINEERING PART NUMBERS
4.1 An operation is a step required to completing a task. A router is a sequence ofoperations
required to complete a work order.
4.2 Appendix A lists the complete routers used on engineering work orders.
4.2.1 Documents created by HPM.
4.2.2 Each table lists (from left to right) the following information:
• Operation number
• Description ofthe operation
• Person responsible for performing the move ticket on that operation
• When the move ticket is to be performed
4.3 The scope ofwork for an operation is dependent upon the operation description. An
attempt is made to keep operation numbers consistent for each operation description.
However, sometimes this can not be done. Care should be taken to follow the operation
description.
5.0 OPERATION SCOPE OF WORK
5.1 LAYOUT
• This covers the creation ofinformal layouts, ifrequired, that facilitate the detailing of
the assembly components.
• It includes the checking and scrubbing ofthose layouts, ifrequired.
5.2 HPMREV-X
• Revisions performed by HPM personnel after a document has been issued as complete.
• X indicates the type oftask being revised. (as listed in table 1)

6.0 REVISIONS
6.1 There are many different types ofrevisions that can be handled in a number ofways. The
manner in which a particular revision is handled directly affects how time charges and
move tickets are done. The following are guidelines for how to handle revisions.
Production Engineering and the Drafting Supervisor will make the final decision on a case­
by-case basis.
6.2 In these instructions, the cause ofthe revision does not matter. These instructions will hold
whether the revision is a customer revision or a detailing error.
6.3 Types ofrevisions
6.3.1 Revisions to Assemblies Before Detailing Starts
6.3.2 Design Change Before Initial Issue
6.3.3 Changes After Drawing Has Been Issued
6.3.4 Approval Drawing Mark-Ups
6.4 A revision that comes prior to the start ofdetailing will not affect the work orders. Simply
start the drawing, charging time and doing move tickets normally, with the latest design.
6.5 Refer to the chapter on 'Operation Scope ofWork' above for where to charge time for
revisions that occur before and after the first issue (including approval mark-ups).
6.6 When a revision is required, Production Engineering and the Drafting Supervisor should be
notified. They should be made aware ofthe exact nature and scope ofthe change. RPM
Engineering and Drafting should charge their time on the proper 'REVISION'-operation.

3.0 STEPS FOR REQUESTING PARTS
3.1 For Fan Engineering or Non-Engineering departments:
3.1.1 Check the Visibility~ Part Master for existing parts. Ifno part exists that matches
your requirements, you will need to request a new part. The PMA can help you
with part descriptions.
3.1.2 Use the procedures outlined in 3.1.3 and 3.1.4 to open the Part Number Request
Form (pNRF). You will need access to FileMaker Pro~. Ifyou do not have
access to this application, contact the HPC Help Desk.
3.1.3 Mac users:
3.1.3.1 Launch the FileMaker Pro~ application.
3.1.3.2 Select 'Open' (0) in the File menu
3.1.3.3 Select the 'Network' button.
3.1.3.4 Select the 'HEC ENET Backbone' zone and double-click 'Part
Number Form'.
3.1.3.5 Select the 'OK' button in the password dialogue box. No password is
required to request a new part.
3.1.4 PC users:
3.1.4.1 Launch the FileMaker Pro~ application.
3.1.4.2 Select 'Open' in the File menu.
3.1.4.3 Select the 'HOSTS' button.
3.1.4.4 Position the mouse pointer over 'Part Number Form.FP3' and double ­
click the left mouse button.
3.1.4.5 Select the 'OK' button in the password dialogue box. No password is
required to request a new part.
3.1.4.6 Resize the window to full screen so that you can view the entire form.
3.1.5 Select 'New Record' in the Mode menu to create a new sheet for your part. Each
new part requested will need a new sheet created (Le., 20 parts will require 20
PNRFs). You must create a new record to prevent the loss o/previously entered
PNRFs.
3.1.6 Fill in the following fields. The part description should be in a format consistent
with existing parts and should uniquely describe the requested part.
3.1.6.1 Department
3.1.6.2 Initiated by
3.1.6.3 Part Description (Users)
3.1.6.4 Material Specifications (If Applicable)

3.2.1 The BOM Administrator should send a completed and checked Skeleton BOM
Request Form to the PMA. This should be done using electronic mail. Refer to
Skeleton BOMRequest Form in Standards Book I, section 4D.
3.3 For ACHE piece-mark parts (shipping and template marks)
3.3.1 Section leaders send checked drawings to Document Control.
3.3.2 Document Control gives a copy ofthe drawing to the PMA.
3.3.3 PMA enters the parts into Visibility~ and returns the drawing to Document
Control.
3.4 For ACHE purchased parts:
3.4.1 Drafting will send a list of the new parts to the PMA.
3.4.2 The PMA will create a PNRF, per 3.1, for each part required.
3.4.2 The PMA will give the new part number back to drafting.
4.0 STEPS FOR THE PMA
4.1 Verify that the requested part is not already in the Visibility~ Part Master.
4.2 After receiving notification that new parts are required, refer to 3.0, enter the information
per paragraphs 5.0 through 12.0 into the Visibility~ Part Master.
4.3 Contact all necessary parties to enter the necessary information per paragraphs 5.0 through
12.0.

5.0 PART MASTER MAINTENANCE SCREEN
5.1 Field 01 Part Number
5.1.1 Manufactured Fan Parts or Purchased Parts:
Assign a 5 digit, non-significant number to the part. Use a sequential report of all
numeric parts in Visibility~ to eliminate the guesswork in assigning the next
sequential part number.
5.1.2 Fan Assemblies:
Use the assembly part number from the PNRF description.
5.1.3 Skeleton BOM Parts:
Part numbers should be per the Skeleton BaM Request Fonn.
5.1.4 ACHE Piece-mark Parts:
Part number = Job No + Dwg No + Piece-mark; separate each with a hyphen
5.2 Field 02 Description
5.2.1 Assign a structured part description.
5.2.2 Refer to the following procedures for most description fonnats.
ETO Part and Assembly Description Structure in Standards Book I, section 4B
Bill ofMaterial Creation in Standards Book I, section 3B
5.2.3 If a new part does not fall into the defined scope ofthese other procedures, refer
to similar parts already in the Part Master. Copy this fonnat as closely as
possible.
5.2.4 Ifthere is not a part in the Part Master similar to the new one, determine the part's
characteristics (descriptive noun, material type, specs, dimensions, etc.) and make
a new structured fonnat.
5.3 Field 03 Drawing Revision (default; see 10.1)
5.4 Field 04 Make or Buy Code = B for purchased parts, M for manufactured parts.
5.5 Field 05 Unit of Measure
5.5.1 Look for a part with a similar commodity code.
5.5.2 Set UoM to equal the part with the similar commodity code.
5.5.3 If there is no similar part, consult with Inventory Control, Engineering, and
Purchasing for suggestions. After consulting with these departments, make a
decision and set the UoM.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 4B -PG. 1
DESCRIPTIONS OF ENGINEER-TO-ORDER PARTS
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 This document defines the description structure for ETO parts that will receive a part
number. These descriptions will be shown on the drawing BOM and in Visibility for each
part number.
1.2 ETO parts are separated into two types of parts, each with its own description format.
1.2.1 Assemblies and Non-Welded Components
1.2.2 Welded Components
1.3 ETO descriptions are to be maintained by the PMA. The Standards Department and
Production Engineering will maintain this procedure.
1.4 This procedure does NOT cover descriptions for the following part numbers.
1.4.1 Skeleton BOM parts, discussed in Bill ofMaterials Creation in Standards Book 1,
section 3B.
1.4.2 Purchased parts, which are maintained by the PMA
1.4.3 Standard parts, which are maintained by the Standards Department
2.0 CONTENTS
1.0 PURPOSE 1
2.0 CONTENTS 1
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS 1
4.0 DESCRIPTION TABLES FOR COMMON ETO PARTS AND ASSEMBLIES 2
5.0 PARTS NOT LISTED IN TABLES 10
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 Work this procedure with Bill ofMaterials Creation in Standards Book I, section 3B, and
Standards Book II sections for each drawing series.
DESCRIPTIONS OF ENGINEER-TO-ORDER PARTS REV. 3, 3-22-02
Data Issued
By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0

*2414807-0*
I I I I
STD BOOK HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION SECT. 4B -PG. 2
3.2 This procedure is the primary source for ETO descriptions. The descriptions shown on
reference drawings and in other procedures and work instructions are NOT necessarily up­
to-date. In cases of conflict, the descriptions in this procedure will take precedence.
4.0 DESCRIPTION TABLES FOR COMMON ETO PARTS AND ASSEMBLIES
4.1 The tables are configured per drawing series.
4.2 Italic text in the tables references infonnation required when a description is entered. This
infonnation may vary from part to part. The rest of the description is entered as shown.
4.3 All dimensions should be shown in fractional fonn.
4.4 All lengths should be shown in feet and inches and all other dimensions in inches. Include
a foot symbol but not an inch symbol.
4.5 Material thickness (only for pressed channel tube spacers) is shown in fractional inches
unless a gauge material is used.
4.6 Length and width dimensions offonned objects (i.e., bent, rolled, pressed, etc.) should be
shown as pre-fonned dimensions. This gives the actual lengths and widths required to start
fabrication.
4.7 All other dimensions (except for the pressed channel tube spacers) should be shown in the
detail.
4.8 Assemblies and Non-Welded Components
4.8.1 Assemblies are objects composed of two or more components that are joined
together.
4.8.2 Non-welded components are objects composed only of the raw material and are
bolted to other objects to fonn assemblies. These components can also be placed
into other assemblies without being bolted or welded.
4.8.3 The following welded components will be treated like non-welded components
for description purposes.
a. Side air seals that are tack welded to the side channel of the frame
b. Plate components that make up or are welded to the header box
c. Stiffeners in nozzles
4.8.4 Descriptions for non-welded components made from plate or sheet (or other
material stocked in units of square feet), should also include ",width x length" at
the end of the description listed.
4.8.5 Descriptions for assemblies, non-welded components, and the welded component
exceptions listed above can be found in the following tables.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 4B -PG. 10
5.0 PARTS NOT LISTED IN TABLES
5.0 Situations will arise when an ETO part is not listed on any ofthe tables. Ifthe part is a
welded component, a new description format must be added to table 7. Otherwise, the
format should be added at the discretion of Production Engineering.
5.1 The following steps should be followed when adding a description format.
5.1.1 A request for a new description format is submitted to the PMA.
5.1.2 The PMA will construct a new description format for this part. This new
description format is created with purchased and standard part descriptions in
mind. The PMA will need to know the identity and function of the part.
5.1.3 The new description format is submitted to Production Engineering for review.
5.1.4 Production Engineering will coordinate with the Standards Department to add the
new format to the appropriate table and to reissue this procedure.

PART MASTER CHANGES
1.0 PURPOSE
1.1 This procedure first lists the types ofchanges that it covers.
1.2 It assigns authority to those individuals who can make change request to the PMA.
1.3 It outlines the procedure for changing the Part Master.
1.4 It outlines a procedures for clean-up and maintenance ofthe Part Master.
1.5 Table 1 defines the nomenclature used in this document.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT.4C-PG.2
3.0 TYPES OF CHANGES
3.1 Adding a part to the PM
3.2 Deleting a part from the PM
3.3 Changing any portion of a part's description
3.4 Changing basic part parameters (fields 03 - 09) in the PM Maintenance screen
3.5 Changing Engineering Control information
3.6 Changing Purchasing Control information
3.7 Changing Inventory Control information
3.8 Changing Sales & Financial Control information
3.9 Creating and maintaining parts for special circumstances such as tests and new product
lines
4.0 AUTHORITY FOR REQUEST
4.1 The following paragraphs assign authority for making a change request to the PMA. All
individuals requiring a change must contact the person(s) assigned below.
4.2 TQM teams may make requests directly to the PMA.
4.3 Adding a Part to the PM
4.3.1 Skeletal BOM assemblies are requested by Production Engineering. This includes
any "Main" assemblies that are added after the original Skeletal BOM has been
created. Subcontracted assemblies are included here.
4.3.2 Drawing part numbers are requested by Production Engineering.
4.3.3 "Make" parts detailed on Revision 0 documents are requested by the section
leaders.
4.3.4 "Make" parts added or changed on Revision 1+ documents are requested by the
BOM Administrator.
4.3.5 "Buy" parts are requested by section leaders or Purchasing.
4.3.6 Standard parts will be requested by the Standard Detpartment.
4.4 Deleting a Part from the PM
4.4.1 Production Engineering will make all requests for deleting parts.
4.4.2 No "Buy" part shall be deleted from the PM unless it was entered in error and
NEVER used on a BOM, work order, or purchase order. Those which have been
used, will be made obsolete. These will go through the Production Engineers too.
4.5 Changing a Part's Description
4.5.1 Description changes for "Buy" parts should be requested by a section leader (or a
header designer for pressure parts).
4.5.2 Changes to "Main" assemblies are to be requested by Production Engineering.
PART MASTER CHANGES REV. 0, 12-15-98

5.0 CHANGING THE PART MASTER
5.1 Revisions to descriptions should be handled by submitting a PD CRF as described in
Engineering/Drafting Revisions in the Engineering Standards Book I, section 6.
5.2 Changes to any ofthe other settings for a given part should be handled by sending a written
request to the PMA. Electronic mail will be sufficient notification.
5.3 Adding parts to the PM should be handled in one ofthe following ways.
5.3.1 Part Request Form
5.3.2 Submitting a drawing with a list of new parts
5.3.3 Electronic mail
5.4 Deletion ofparts will require written notification. Electronic mail is sufficient.
6.0 PART MASTER CLEAN-UP PROCEDURES
6.1 This is a procedure for removing parts that are not being used.
6.2 This process will begin with a clean-up and continue with a monthly review.
6.3 The clean-up process will begin with the creation ofan Impromptu~ report.
6.3.1 This report will list parts that do not have a 'where used' and have not been
adjusted within the past 30 days.
6.3.2 The following fields will appear on this report.
Part Number
i
Level
Revised Date.
6.3.3 A filter will be applied to the 'Level' and to the 'Revised Date'. Only level 01
and dates prior to 30 days before printing will be included on the report.
6.3.4 The file for this report will be 'Parts Flagged fur Deletion'. It can be found in the
'Section 4' directory of Standards Book I. Refer to the Standards Book I Index.
6.3.5 That report will be linked to the catalog, 'Engineering - General'. This catalog
can be found in the following directory:
N:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting
6.4 There are some parts that are not used anywhere for fabrication but have been setup for
reference purposes only.
6.4.1 Some examples are the router templates.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 4C -PG. 6
6.4.2 Each department manager will furnish a list ofthese parts to the BOM
Administrator.
6.4.3 The BOM Administrator will create and maintain a BOM for a part called
'PART-SP' that will group these reference parts.
6.4.4 'PART-SP' will be excluded from the Impromptu~ search.
6.5 The procedure for the removal of unused parts is as follows. The clean-up will follow the
same procedure.
6.5.1 The PMA will run the 'Parts Flagged For Deletion' report once per month and
flag potential candidates. Some can easily be removed from consideration such as
job part numbers, and bank part numbers after the clean-up.
6.5.2 The PMA will view each part in the Inquiry screen and check to see if each part
has any ofthe following data. Ifso, that part will be removed from consideration.
'BOM
Sales Orders
Purchase Orders
Warehouse History
Material Requirements
6.5.3 The PMA will compile a list of parts to be considered for deletion and present that
list to Production Engineering.
6.5.4 Production Engineering will research each part to ensure that it has not been used
and is not scheduled for future use. Ifa fan part is on the list, Production
Engineering will contact the Fan Engineering Group to determine ifit can be
deleted.
6.5.5 Production Engineering will return to the PMA a list ofthe parts that need to be
deleted.
6.5.6 The PMA will delete the necessary part. Production Engineering will contact
those affected, if necessary.

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 4D - PG. 2
3.0 CREATING THE SKELETON HOM
3.1 You will need the following documents before starting.
3.1.1 FFSS
3.1.2 Proposal Drawing
3.1.3 Copy of the Job Number Request from the Project Coordinator, usually
distributed via electronic mail.
3.1.4 Kickoff meeting notes
3.2 Following the steps in paragraph 4.0, generate a complete skeleton BOM.
3.3 Submit a hard copy of the Skeleton BOM Request Form to Production Engineering.
3.4 Production Engineering will check the BOM against the documents listed in 3.1. The
BOM will be checked for skeleton structure and part descriptions.
3.5 Make any necessary corrections on the Skeleton BOM Request Form.
3.6 Send the finished request form to the PMA via electronic mail. Copy the following persons
when sending that request.
3.6.1 PP&S Manager
3.6.2 PP&S Personnel responsible for setting up the Work Order BOM
3.6.3 Production Engineer who checked the form
3.7 After the PMA is finished entering all ofthe parts, enter the single-level bills into
Visibility~. Refer to the Visibility~, Engineering User Guide for instructions on performing
this task.
3.8 Submit a printout ofthe BOM from Visibility~ along with the checked copy of the Skeleton
BOM Request Form to the Production Engineer who checked the request form originally.
3.9 The Production Engineer checks the bill for input of bill structure, including quantity, and
for part description input.
4.0 SKELETON HOM REQUEST FORM TEMPLATE
4.1 You will need to copy the file, Master2.dot from the server to your local hard drive.
4.1.1 On the server, this file is located at the following location:
Q:\HPC_CAD_SERVER\STANDARDS & PROCEDURES\Standards Book l\Section 4
4.1.2 It should be copied to the following location in your hard drive:
C:\MSOffice\Templates
4.1.3 This file is updated and kept current by the BOM Administrator. This could
change periodically. Since the BOM Administrator is the only one who uses this
template, the most current copy should always be used. The BOM Administrator
must make sure this file is kept current as skeleton bill structures change.
4.2 Launch the MS Word~ application.
4.3 From the File menu, select 'New'.
SKELETON BOM REQUEST FORM REV. 0, 12-15-98

By: Barnes, Carbrey
Date: 01-09-2025, Rev: 0

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STD BOOK SECT. 4D -PC. 3
4.4 Choose the template, 'Master2'.
4.5 Review the forms listed in 3.1 and determine the quantity of banks, ACHEs, bundles, etc.
required for the job.
4.6 Use the copy and paste functions in Word~ to duplicate as many banks, ACHEs ,etc.
required.
4.7 Please keep in mind that all Banks, ACHEs, etc. should have sequential lettering (i.e.
H545-11A, H545-11B, etc.).
4.7.1 Occasionally, you will come across some jobs in which you might have to get out
of sequence.
4.7.2 The BOM Administrator and Production Engineering will have to make the
determination when to deviate from sequential lettering on assemblies.
4.8 Ifa unit is induced draft, delete H###-5?? and DH###-5?? from the skeleton for that unit.
4.9 The skeleton bill template includes both standard and non-standard shafts.
4.9.1 Ifa unit is induced draft or has non-standard forced draft fan shafts, remove the
standard shaft (pin 04A01) from the skeleton for that unit.
4.9.2 Ifa unit is forced draft with a standard shaft, remove both H###-l01??-1 and
DH###-101A from the skeleton bill for that unit.
4.9.3 Ifa unit is forced draft with non-standard fan shafts, add H###-102??-1 And
DH###-102A in place ofH###-lOl??-1 and DH###-10IA.
4.10 Continue to remove any assemblies and drawings that the FFSS show as not being part of
HPC's scope ofsupply.
4.11 Next use the find and replace functions in Word~ to fill in the complete descriptions and
part numbers for each assembly and drawing. Please refer to the appendix for an
explanation ofeach symbol and what it refers to.
4.12 You will need to use the FFSS to aid you in developing descriptions.
4.13 Once the descriptions have been completed, proceed to enter the correct quantities required
for each assembly, drawing, etc.
4.14 You must also designate any parts that are to be placed on the sal~s order. Do this by
typing 'SO' at the far right side of the line that corresponds to the sales line item part
number.
4.15 For any part that should already be in the Parts Master when it is time to enter, assuming
the PMA goes through the list from top to bottom, type an asterisk (*) to the right of the
parts quantity, or 'SO'.
4.16 Any assembly that is to be manufactured by an outside vendor, should have BUY entered
to the right ofthe quantity onthe line corresponding to the assembly. Ifthe assembly has a
drawing part number associated with it, move the part number up one level in the skeleton
bill.

APPENDIX: FIND AND REPLACE INSTRUCTION
A.I FIND & REPLACE FUNCTION
A.I.I In MS Word~, select 'Replace.. .' from the Edit menu.
A.I.2 Type the symbol, shown in the list in A.2 below, in the 'Find What:' box. Start
with the first symbol in the list and proceed through the list. The last symbol
replaced should be ' •••'. This is for miscellaneous information that depends on
the part.
A.I.3 Type the description text you wish to insert in place of the symbol in the 'Replace
With:' box.
A.I.4 Select the 'Find Next' button.
A.I.5 Select either the 'Replace' or the 'Replace All' button. This will depend on what
you are replacing.
A.I.5.1 Use the 'Replace All' button when replacing ### with the project
number.
A. 1.5.2 Use the 'Replace' button for everything else.
A.I.6 When you select the 'Replace' button, Word~ will automatically find the next
occurrence ofthat symbol.
A.I.6.1 At some point, you will need to change the text in the 'Replace With'
box.
A.I.6.2 The parts will determine when you need to change this text. Some
description information and part number characters can be used on
multiple parts. The number of parts will depend on the project.
A.I.7 Check all 'FIN aD' descriptions for finned-tube parts. The default is set at 2.25
but this may change when the outside diameter of tubes increases above I".
A.I.8 Changethe machinery mount widths from 3'-6" to 2'-6" ifthe fan diameteris less
then 8' for that particular ACHE.
A.I.9 Review the list to make sure unintended copies were not performed. Also review
descriptions that are normally set as default but may require changing because of­
a unique project.
A.I.IO Remember to work this with Bill ofMaterials Creation in Standards Book I,
section 3B.
A.1.11 In the Section 4 directory ofthe Standards Book I directory, refer to Standards
Book I Index, there is a file called, 'Part Description Easy Reference'. This file
gives a swnmary ofdescription formats as found in Bill ofMaterials Creation.
The BaM Administrator will keep this file updated as changes occur. If you print
this file, you may be working with an out dated version so check this file often for
the most current description formats.

each document as completed
1.1.3 To keep track ofthe approval returns with transmittal dates
1.1.4 To keep track ofthe issue date for each docwnent
1.1.5 By Docwnent Control

SID BOOK HUDSONPRODUCTSCORPORATION SECI.S-PG.2
3.0 ASSOCIATED DOCUMENTS
3.1 All documents are listed on the Drawing Schedule
3.2 Customer specification sheets
3.3 All files referenced in this procedure can be found in the following directory:
Q:\HPC_CAD_SERVER\STANDARDS & PROCEDURES\sTANDARD BOOK l\Sect 5\Sheet
Numbers Log
4.0 OWNERSHIP AND ISSUANCE
4.1 The Drawing Schedule is an Excel file, created by the Section Leader and checked by the
Standards Department.
4.2 The Drawing Schedule is issued by electronic mail to Document Control, Scheduling,
MTO, Drafting Supervisor, Production Engineering, and the appropriate Project
Coordinator.
4.3 The Drawing Schedule should be issued within 5 days after the job number is issued.
4.4 When a new document is added or deleted from the Drawing Schedule, it should be
reissued per 4.2.
5.0 COMPUTER
5.1 Using new EXCEL form.
5.1.1 Open the appropriate master file;
MASTER (ND) DIS
MASTER (FD) DIS
MASTER (RT) DIS
5.1.2 Rename the file by saving it as JOB NO-DSI (example: G599-DSI). Save in the
appropriate directory for the project which can be found in the directory:
Q:\HPC_CAD_SERVER\HPC_CAD_JOBS\Checked_ISSUED\
5.2 Computer commands.
5.2.1 INSERT LINE
5.2.1.1 Inserts a range ofcells equivalent in size and shape to the selection,
and shifts the selection to accommodate new cells.
5.2.1.2 To use the INSERT LINE command, click on the row number to
highlight the whole line and use COMMAND (B) 1.
5.2.2 DELETE LINE
5.2.2.1 Removes selected cells from a worksheet and shifts surrounding cells
to fill the space.
5.2.2.2 To use the DELETE LINE command, click on the row number to
highlight the whole line and use COMMAND (9) K.
5.2.3 COpy LINE
5.2.3.1 Copies the selection and places it onto the Clipboard.
5.2.3.2 To use the COpy LINE command, click on the row number to
highlight the whole line and use COMMAND ( 9) C.
5.3 Print set up button at top ofform

5.3.1 This macro only sets the print area and makes the last page full.

6.0 CREATION OF THE DRAWING SCHEDULE
6.1 Work this section with REFERENCE #1, EXAMPLE #1, and EXAMPLE #2 at then end of
Standards Book I, section 5. These samples can also be found in the MS Excel~ files,
REF lORAWINGSCHEDULE, EXP1MASTER(FDND)DS (forced or induced draft units),
and EXP2MASTER(RB)DS (replacement bundles).
6.2 Section Leader initials
6.3 Date Drawing Schedule is first issued
6.4 Customer name and plant location (from FFSS)
6.5 Project Coordinator's, Structural Engineer's and Header Designer's initials (from Job
Package)
6.6 Drawing Schedule revisions
6.6.1 Revision number
6.6.2 Revision date
6.6.3 Revision type (N =new drawing added, R =revised line, 0 = deleted document).
6.7 HPC job number (from FFSS in the Job Package)
6.8 Customer PO Number (from Job Package)
6.9 Drawing number
6.9.1 Use the Document Issue Requirement Chart for abbreviations and HPC document
requirements.
6.9.2 Also see customer data specifications for document requirements.
6.9.3 If there are no customer data specifications, see Job Package for requirements.
6.10 Bankletter ofcorresponding drawing number (put"ALL" ifdocument is for all banks)
6.11 Item number (from FFSS) (put "ALL" ifdocument is for all items)
6.12 Drawing requirements
6.12.1 Customer quantity requirements -- AFPROYAL / FINAL (see customer data
specifications). This lets document control and scheduling know ifthe first issue
(rev. 0) is issued for approval or final. Ifno customer requirements, HPC standard
is to issue fmal to the customer.
6.12.2 Customer quantity requirements -- R =reproducible (see customer data
specifications or HPC standard = 1), P =prints (see customer data specifications
or HPC standard = 3).
6.12.3 No quantities required for HPC documents not issued to the customer (fill in with
"_rt).
6.12.4 Shop issue (-- =not issued to shop (Internal issue only), A= issue to HPC
manufacturing, purchasing or outside fabrication).
6.13 Description -- Use the Document Issue Requirement Chart for the description.

7.0 USING THE DRAWING SCHEDULE
7.1 Work this section with REFERENCE #1 at the end of Standards Book I, section 5. These
samples can also be found in the MS Excel~ file, REFIDRAWINGSCHEDULE.
7.2 Detailer's initials (detailer fill in when detailing starts)

7.4 Checker's initials (checker fill in when checking starts)
7.5 Checker's date (checker fill in when checking is completed and ready to issue)
7.6 Customer approval return with date. (NR)
7.6.1 A =Document returned approved. Check customer transmittal to see ifa reissue
final is required.
7.6.2 R =Drawing or document returned NOT approved. The document needs to be
revised and reissued.
7.7 Date of document issued (revision 0 through 5). For revisions over 5 put in blank line
under document being revised and put date for revision 6 starting in revision 0 column.

STD BOOK SECT. 7A -PG. 1
AUTOMATION DOCUMENTATION
1.0 PURPOSE & INTRODUCTION
1.1 To document all automation procedures in the EngineeringlDrafting department.
1.2 Each chapter of this document will cover one automation routine. The documentation will
include the following items.
1.2.1 instructions for using the routine
1.2.2 instructions for installing the routine on a user's PC
1.2.3 a complete list of computer files that will be used or created by the routine
1.2.4 a detailed make-up of the files used by the routine
1.2.5 a complete reproduction of any program code (macros, scripts, etc.) used by the
routine
1.3 Each section of this document can stand alone and will carry its own revision number and
date. This number and date of issue is located at the lower right-hand side of each page.
1.3.1 The revision number and date on a given page will only apply to that particular
section. The pages will be numbered with the chapter, a hyphen, and the page
number in that section.
1.3.2 Section 1consists only ofthe 'Purpose' ofthis document.
1.3.3 Section 2 consists of the table of contents and has no number associated with the
chapter (only a bullet mark). The pages are numbered in lower case roman
numerals.
1.3.4 Each of the documentation chapters are lettered, starting with A.
1.4 When a section is revised, only that section will be changed and issued. If a revision
causes a change in headings and/or page numbers, the table of contents section will also be
revised and issued.
1.5 An installation log is maintained for each program contained in this document. This log in
a MS Excel file (Automation Installation Log.xls) in the following directory.
q:\HPC_CAD_SERVER\STANDARDS & PROCEDURES\Standards Book I\Section 7 Miscellaneous\
1.6 The installation log gives the date of initial installation for each user, dates of updates, and
the date of the most recent version.
1.7 Copies of all electronic files for each of these automation routines are saved in the
following directory. They are organized in sub-directories by routine.
q:\HPC_CAD_SERVER\STANDARDS & PROCEDURES\Standards Book I\Section 7
Miscellaneous\Automation Program Files

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STDBOOK SECT.7A-PG.B-l
B DRAFTING SCHEDULE GANTT CHART & HEADER DESIGN SCHEDULE
Purpose & Introduction
This automation routine utilizes Impromptu to extract data from Visibility and organize that data, by
drawing, in a schedule format. The routine then imports the Impromptu output (through MS Excel)
into MS Project and organizes the schedule in chronological order. It requires minimal input by the
user.
Instructions for Use
Running the Impromptu Macro:
1. If the shortcut for the macro has been installed on your desktop, double-click the 'sched.mac'
shortcut. Then proceed to step 2. Otherwise, skip steps 1 through 3 and proceed to step 4.
2. Press the 'F5' key and then skip to step 5.
3. This macro will do the following:
3.1. run all necessary Impromptu reports
3.2. create the appropriate MS Excel file (wl1.xls)
3.3. run and print the Header Design Schedule to the default printer
3.4. close Impromptu
3.5. launch MS Project
4. You can also run the macro from within Impromptu by selecting 'Macro...', from the 'Tools'
menu. Then select the file, 'sched.mac' (extension may not appear depending on your
computer's configuration), in the following directory:
c:\Cognos\Bi97\User Workspace\Drafting Schedule\
Finish this method by selecting the 'Run' button.
5. Retrieve the Header Design Schedule from the default printer for your Pc.
Updating the MS Project File:
1. The Microsoft Project file, Drafting Schedule.mpp, is on the server and is available for anyone
to access at any time. This file must not be open on anyone's PC or this program will not work
properly. You may want to open the file first. If you get any 'read-only' notices, the file is
open on someone's Pc. Otherwise, close the file and proceed with the next step.
2. IfMS Project is running from the server on your PC, open the file,
n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Schedule\Schedule Macro.mpp. Otherwise, skip this and
the next two steps then proceed to step 5.
3. Microsoft Project will warn you that the file contains macros. Select the 'Enable Macros'
button.
4. Type 'Ctrl-T'. Skip step 5 and proceed to step 6.
5. Type 'Ctrl-Q'.
6. You will receive the following warning message:
The selection is too large.
Microsoft Project may not be able to undo changes made to such a large selection.
Do you want to continue anyway?
7. Select the 'Yes' button or press [Enter].

10. You will then receive another warning message:
A pasting error occurred on ID 1 in the Number 1 column.
The number you entered is invalid or is outside the range for a number field.
Make sure you are typing only numbers and no letters in this field, or type a smaller
number.
To continue pasting with additional error messages, click Yes.
To continue pasting with no error messages, click No.
To stop the paste operation, click Cancel.
11. Select the 'No' button or press [Tab] then [Enter].
12. Print the chart on llxI7-paper.
13. Close Microsoft Project 98.
Program Installation
Impromptu User Version Installation
1 Copy the following files to the directory c:\Cognos\Bi97\User Workspace\Drafting
Schedule\ on the user's Pc.

n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Schedule\Sched.mcx

3 Open the file wl2.imr from the user's PC (not the server copy).
4 Log-in to the catalog when prompted.
5 The system wants you to copy the catalog to the local hard drive. Save it as Hotfiles to the
default directory for that Pc.
6 Link wl2.imr to this new copy ofthe Hotfiles catalog.
7 Save and close wl2.imr.
8 Open wl2.imr again (the system will notify you that it needs to reestablish links to the new
catalog), press OK, save the file and then close it.
9 Open and save w13.imr, wI4.imr, wI5.imr, and HDSched.imr in order.
10 Close the Hotfiles catalog.
11 Open each ofthese reports again to ensure the new links were established. Be sure to close the
catalog before opening & testing the next report.
12 Open wll.imr and log-in to the catalog when requested.

STD BOOK SECT. 7A -PG. B-4
2. Test each Impromptu report wll.imr through w15.imr and HDSched.imr individually, per step
11 above. You should not have to save a copy ofeither ofthe two catalogs.
3. Create a shortcut to the Impromptu macro and save it on the desktop.
4. Modify rows 25 and 56 ofthe Impromptu macro as follows:
4.1. replace "FILE" with "n:\transferfolder\drafting\schedule\hotfiles.cat" in row 25
4.2. replace "FILE" with "n:\transferfolder\drafting\schedule\Drafting Schedule.cat"
in row 56
4.3. replace "VER" with "creator"
4.4. replace "ID" with the UserID ofthat particular administrator
4.5. replace "PW" with the Password of that particular administrator
5. On row 70 ofthe Impromptu macro, replace the directory for 'winproj.exe' ifMS Project is not
accessed from the directory 'c:\Program Files\Microsoft Office\Office\'.
6. Test the Impromptu macro from Impromptu then the shortcut.
7. Ifthe user is running MS Project from the server, skip steps 8 through 22.
8. Open Microsoft Project.
9. From the 'Tools' menu, select 'Macro ~ Macros... Alt +F8'.
10. In the 'Macro Name:' box, type 'Drafting_Schedule', then select the 'Create' button.
11. Open Notepad.
12. From the 'File' menu, select 'Open...'.
13. Select the following file and select the 'Open' button:
n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Schedule\Microsoft Project Macro - Drafting Schedule.txt
14. Select all text in this text file.
15. From the 'Edit' menu, select 'Copy'.
16. Active the Microsoft Visual Basic window and select all text.
17. From 'Edit' menu, select 'Paste'.
18. Save the Microsoft Project macro then close notepad and Microsoft Visual Basic.
19. In Microsoft Project, open the macros list per step 9 above.
20. Select 'DraftinILSchedule', then select the 'Options' button.
21. In the 'Shortcut Key' box at the bottom ofthe 'Macro Options' window, type a 'Q' then
select the 'OK' button.
22. Select the 'Close' button.
23. Test the Microsoft Project macro from within Microsoft Project. Microsoft Excel should not
be running and the 'Drafting Schedule.mpp' file should be closed.

Macros
1. Impromptu
n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Schedule\Sched.mac
(n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Schedule\Sched.mcx is created by the compiler)
This macro can be accessed using the CognosScript Editor and is reprinted here:
'This Routine will run the following Impromptu reports and save each as
'the hot files shown below. These hot files will be used to run the
'drafting workload report.
'WORKLOAD - DETAIL & START (w12.imr) hot file - WL2
'WORKLOAD - CHECK (w13.imr) hot file - WL3
'WORKLOAD - SCRUB (w14.imr) hot file - WL4
'WORKLOAD - ISSUE & FINISH (w15.imr) hot file - WL5
'The routine will also run the following Impromptu report and print it.
'Header Design Schedule (HDSched.imr)
'All ofthese files can be found in c:\Cognos\Bi97\User Workspace\Schedule\
DIM ImpromptuApp As Object
DIM ImpromptuReport As Object
DIM TaskID as Integer
Sub Main
'Set the Impromptu Application Object
Set ImpromptuApp = CreateObject ("Impromptu.Application.30")
'Open the hot file catalog
ImpromptuApp.OpenCatalog "FILE","VER"""ID","PW"
'Run Header Design Schedule
Set ImpromptuReport = ImpromptuApp.OpenReport ("c:\Cognos\Bi97\User
Workspace\Drafting Schedule\HDSched.imr")
ImpromptuReport.Print
ImpromptuReport.CloseReport
'Run WORKLOAD - DETAIL & START
Set ImpromptuReport = ImpromptuApp.OpenReport ("c:\Cognos\Bi97\User
Workspace\Drafting Schedule\w12.imr")
ImpromptuReport.ExportHotFile "n:\transfer\drafting\schedule\w12.ims"
ImpromptuReport.CloseReport
'Run WORKLOAD - CHECK
Set ImpromptuReport = ImpromptuApp.OpenReport ("c:\Cognos\Bi97\User
Workspace\Drafting Schedule\w13.imr")
ImpromptuReport.ExportHotFile "n:\transfer\drafting\schedule\w13.ims"

ImpromptuReport.CloseReport
'Run WORKLOAD - SCRUB

Workspace\Drafting Schedule\wI4.imr")
ImpromptuReport.ExportHotFile "n:\transfer\drafting\schedule\wI4.ims"

I I I I
HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STDBOOK SECT.7A-PG.C-l
C COST & WEIGHT CALCULATION AND ENTRY
Purpose & Introduction
The purpose ofthis program is to quickly calculate the weights and costs of sub-contracted structural
assemblies and enter those values into Visibility.
Instructions For Use
1 There are some things that must be done and information that must be gathered prior to
executing the script.
1.1 All parts, assembly and components, need to be entered into Visibility with the proper
settings. Some ofthe more important settings are:
1.1.1 Make / Buy flag
1.1.2 Phantom flag
1.1.3 Engineering Category
1.2 The complete bills ofmaterials should be entered and checked first.
1.3 Ifthe vendor is anyone other than RPM, the file
'n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Sublets\Outside Sublet Pricing.xIs needs to be set up
with the project and proper costs. The data for the project that is the focus ofthe current
run should be in column 3 ofthe appropriate worksheet. Production Engineering should
enter the prices into this file.
1.4 You will need the part number of the assembly for which component assemblies will be
sub-contracted.
1.5 You will need to know whether or not there are revised cost records for the sub-contracted
assemblies. Either all must have them or all must not have them. Ifsome, but not all have
them, you will need to create the revised cost records, manually, for those that don't. To
check for these records, follow these steps from the main menu in Visibility:
1.5.1 Type PC and <ENTER>
1.5.2 Type 03 and <ENTER>
1.5.3 Type F and <ENTER>
1.5.4 Type the part number of the assembly, followed by @ and <ENTER>.
1.5.5 Press <ENTER> several times. If only the assembly part number appears, then
none of the parts have revised cost records. Otherwise, at least some have them
(check that all do).
1.6 You will need to know the name of the vendor.
1.7 If the vendor is RPM, you will need to know ifthe assemblies are to be galvanized or
painted.
2 Position the cursor, in Visibility, in the 'Selection:' field in the 'Main Menu'.
3 If an icon has been set up in your copy of Reflections, select with the mouse. Ifnot, select Run
Script from the Script menu in Reflections.
4 Select the script file WCEntryU.rbs or WCEntryA.rbs, depending on your particular setup (the
extension' .rbs' may not appear, depending on your PC's settings).
5 Select the Run button.
6 Follow the instructions in the various dialogue boxes that will appear.
6.1 This program performs three different tasks.
6.1.1 Calculate and enter the weights of sub-contracted assembly components.
AUTOMATION DOCUMENTATION REV. 0,3-6-00

By: Barnes, Carbrey

HUDSON PRODUCTS CORPORATION
STDBOOK SECT.7A-PG.C-2
6.1.2 Calculate and enter the weights of sub-contracted assemblies.
6.1.3 Calculate and enter the costs of sub-contracted assemblies.
6.2 The program will need to be run three times for each assembly in the following order. If
this order is not followed, the final costs will not be correct.
6.2.1 Weights - for components
6.2.2 Weights - for assemblies
6.2.3 Costs
6.3 When entering the part number for the assembly, be sure to use all capital letters.
Visibility Screen Access Required
You are required to have access to the following screens and processes in order to run this report.
MENU ENMENU PCMENU
EN050 EN05D PC020

Program Installation
Impromptu User Version Installation
1 Copy the following files to the directory c:\Cognos\Bi97\User Workspace\Sublets\ on the user's
PC.
n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Sublets\CostData.imr
n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Sublets\CompWght.imr
n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Sublets\AssyWght.imr
2 Copy the following file to the default, script directory on the user's Pc.
n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\Drafting\Sublets\WCEntry.rbs
3 Change the name ofWCEntry.rbs to WCEntryU.rbs.
4 Launch the Impromptu application.
5 Open the report, CostData.imr from the user's PC (not the server copy).
6 Log-in to the catalog when prompted.
7 The system wants you to copy the catalog to the local hard drive. If the catalog
'Engineering-General' already exists on the user's PC, save the catalog as 'Temporary.cat' to
the default directory, for that PC. Otherwise, save it as 'Engineering-General' in the
directory, c:\Cognos\Bi97\User Workspace\Sublets\.
8 Link the report to the 'Engineering-General' catalog on the user's PC (note the directory as it
will be used later when modifying the script).
9 Save and close the report. Then close the catalog.
10 Open that same report again (the system will notify you that it will reestablish links to the
new catalog), press OK, save the report and then close it (leaving the PC version of the
catalog open).
11 Open the report, CompWght.imr from the user's PC (not the server copy).
12 Save the report and close it (leaving the PC version of the catalog open).
13 Repeat steps 11 and 12 for the report, AssyWghtimr.
14 Close the 'Engineering-General' catalog.
15 Open each of these reports again to ensure the new links were established. Be sure to close
the catalog before opening & testing each report.
16 Close Impromptu.

Option Explicit
I ~------------------------------------- _
,-----SUB-PROGRAM TO CALCULATE & ENTER WEIGHTS OF COMPONENT PARTS-------------­
,-----------------------------------------------------------------------------­
Sub WEIGHTCOMP (ASSY,CR)
Dim PART As String
Dim WEIGHT As Single
Dim Excel As Object
Dim PartCell As String
Dim WeightCell As String
Dim ROW As Integer
Dim NextPart As string
Dim IMPROMPTU As Object
Dim ImpReport As Object
'-----IMPROMPTU CALCULATES WEIGHTS OF COMPONENT PARTS & SAVES AS EXCEL--------­
Set IMPROMPTU = CreateObject ("Impromptu.Application")
IMPROMPTU.OpenCatalog "n:\transferfolder\drafting\engineering - general.cat","??CLASS??",,"??ID??","??PASSWORD??"
Set ImpReport = IMPROMPTU.OpenReport ("c:\ Cognos\Bi97\User Workspace\Sublets\CompWght. imr"', ASSY)
ImpReport.ExportExcel "n:\TRANSFERFOLDER\drafting\sublets\partwgt.xls"
ImpReport.CloseReport
Set ImpReport = Nothing
Set IMPROMPTU = Nothing
'-----MOVE CURSOR TO START POSITION IN VISIBILITY-----------------------------­
Application.Transmit "EN" & CR
Application.Transmit "1" & CR
'-----OPEN EXCEL FILE THAT HAS THE WEIGHTS------------------------------------­
Set Excel = CreateObject ("Excel.Application")
Excel.Workbooks.Open FileName:="\\HPC_HOUSTON\VOL2\PRODUCTS\TRANSFERFOLDER\DRAFTING\Sublets\partwgt.xls"
'-----EXTRACT piN AND WEIGHT FROM EXCEL THEN ENTER INTO VISIBILITY------------­
ROW = 2
Do Until Row = 1000
PartCell '" "A" & Trim$ (Str$ (ROW) )
WeightCell", "F" & Trim$(Str$(ROW»
PART = Excel.Range(PartCell)
WEIGHT", Excel.Range(WeightCell)
If PART = "ZZZ" Then
Exit Do
End IF
WITH APPLICATION

Goto Stop2:

.Transmit nAn & CR

'-----SUB-PROGRAM TO CALCULATE AND ENTER COST OF ASSEMBLIES-------------------­
,-----------------------------------------------------------------------------­
Sub COST (SELECTION,ASSY,CR)
Dim Excel As Object
Dim ROW As Integer
Dim COUNT As Integer
Dim RATE As Double
Dim RateCell As String
Dim PART() As String
Dim CATEGORY () As String
Dim WEIGHT() As Double
Dim PARTTEST As String
Dim COST () As Double
Dim GALVENIZE As Integer
Dim COSTSHEET As String
Dim PROJECT As String
Dim IMPROMPTU As Object
Dim ImpReport As Object
Dim PartCell As String
Dim WeightCell As String
Dim CategoryCell As String
Dim REVISEDCOST As Integer
Dim i As Integer
Dim j As Integer
Dim k As Integer
Dim TestcatCell As String
Dim TESTCAT As String
Dim PROJECTTEST As String
Dim RECORDEXIST As Integer
'-----DETERMINE IF THERE ARE REVISED COST RECORDS-----------------------------­
REVISEDCOST = MsgBox ("Do revised cost records exist?", 3)
If REVISEDCOST = 2 Then
MsgBox "The program will terminate. Please determine if there are revised cost records and then rerun the script.",O
Exit Sub
End If
'-----USER SELECTS A VENDOR---------------------------------------------------­
Begin Dialog VendorDialogue 380,64,"VENDOR"
ButtonGroup.SELECT
Text 20,10,160,28,"Choose a vendor."
Button 20,46,70,14,"HPM"
Button 110,46,70,14,"PREMIER"
